omprehensive LH-LLM Development and Debugging Guide
I've created a complete guide to help implement and debug the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM). This guide is detailed enough that another LLM can help you with troubleshooting at every stage of development.
Key Components Covered in the Guide:
1. Environment Setup

Detailed conda environment creation with specific package versions
CUDA compatibility verification procedures
Comprehensive dependency installation instructions

2. Core Module Implementation

Configuration system with hierarchical parameters
DNA encoding with Evo-2 and HEDGES constraints
Harmonic Processing Units with quantum-inspired dynamics
Digital cell organelles mimicking biological functions
Graph-based communication structures
Neural controller with transformer architecture
Self-organized criticality systems

3. Integration Testing

Component-by-component testing procedures
Full model integration validation
Memory profiling and optimization

4. Training Pipeline

Diffusion evolution optimization implementation

"""
This document provides a comprehensive development and debugging guide for implementing
the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM). It contains detailed instructions and 
debugging tips for each component.
"""

# LH-LLM: Complete Development and Debugging Guide

This guide provides step-by-step instructions for implementing the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM) with extensive debugging information to help troubleshoot common issues throughout the development process.

## Table of Contents

1. [Environment Setup](#1-environment-setup)
2. [Core Modules Implementation](#2-core-modules-implementation)
3. [Integration Testing](#3-integration-testing)
4. [Training Pipeline](#4-training-pipeline)
5. [System Evaluation](#5-system-evaluation)
6. [Common Issues and Solutions](#6-common-issues-and-solutions)

## 1. Environment Setup

### 1.1 Creating a Conda Environment

```bash
conda create -n lhllm python=3.9
conda activate lhllm
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Conda environment creation fails.
  - Check Python version availability with `conda search python`
  - Verify conda is updated with `conda update -n base -c defaults conda`

### 1.2 Installing Dependencies

```bash
# Install PyTorch with CUDA support
pip install torch==2.0.1 torchvision torchaudio --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cu118

# Install graph-related packages
pip install torch-geometric==2.3.1 networkx==3.1

# Install scientific computing packages
pip install scipy==1.11.2 numpy==1.24.3 pandas==2.0.3

# Install visualization packages
pip install matplotlib==3.7.2 plotly==5.15.0 

# Install optimizer and utilities
pip install lion-pytorch==0.1.2 einops==0.6.1 opt_einsum==3.3.0

# Install other utilities
pip install tqdm==4.65.0 psutil==5.9.5
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: CUDA compatibility issues with PyTorch
  - Check CUDA version with `nvidia-smi`
  - Match PyTorch version accordingly (visit pytorch.org)
  - Verify installation with `python -c "import torch; print(torch.cuda.is_available())"`

- **Issue**: Missing/incompatible packages
  - Check package conflicts with `pip check`
  - Try installing problematic packages separately

### 1.3 Evo-2 Installation (Optional)

```bash
# Clone repository
git clone https://github.com/ArcInstitute/evo2.git
cd evo2
pip install -e .
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Evo-2 installation fails
  - This is an expected potential issue as Evo-2 may not be publicly available
  - Implement the mock version defined in the DNA module
  - Verify mock implementation with test cases

### 1.4 CUDA Verification

```python
import torch

def verify_cuda():
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        print(f"CUDA is available")
        print(f"Current CUDA device: {torch.cuda.current_device()}")
        print(f"CUDA device name: {torch.cuda.get_device_name(0)}")
        print(f"CUDA device count: {torch.cuda.device_count()}")
        
        # Test CUDA operation
        x = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        y = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        z = torch.matmul(x, y)
        print(f"CUDA operation successful. Result shape: {z.shape}")
        
        # Test complex tensor support
        complex_tensor = torch.complex(torch.rand(10, 10).cuda(), torch.rand(10, 10).cuda())
        print(f"Complex tensor on CUDA created. Shape: {complex_tensor.shape}")
        
        return True
    else:
        print("CUDA is not available")
        return False

verify_cuda()
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: CUDA shows available but operations fail
  - Restart kernel/Python interpreter
  - Check for CUDA out-of-memory errors
  - Verify CUDA driver and toolkit compatibility

- **Issue**: Complex tensors not supported
  - Ensure PyTorch version >= 1.9 for complex tensor support
  - Fallback to real tensors and manual complex arithmetic if needed

## 2. Core Modules Implementation

### 2.1 Directory Structure Creation

Create the following structure for the project:

```bash
mkdir -p lhllm/{config,models,training,utils,data,scripts}
touch lhllm/__init__.py
touch lhllm/{config,models,training,utils,data,scripts}/__init__.py
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Import errors after creating structure
  - Ensure `__init__.py` files exist in each directory
  - Add project root to PYTHONPATH: `export PYTHONPATH=$PYTHONPATH:/path/to/project`

### 2.2 Configuration Module

File: `lhllm/config/configuration.py`

**Key Implementation Points:**
- Use Python dataclasses for configuration
- Include parameters for all model components
- Provide methods for saving/loading configurations
- Implement parameter validation

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Configuration loading fails
  - Check JSON file format and encoding
  - Verify all required fields are present
  - Handle type conversions explicitly

- **Issue**: Config parameter validation fails
  - Add more detailed logging
  - Implement validation in `__post_init__`
  - Add specific error messages for each validation rule

### 2.3 DNA Module Testing

Test the DNA module implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder

def test_sequence_generation():
    config = LHLLMConfig()
    encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    
    # Generate sequence
    sequence = encoder.generate_sequence("Test prompt", n_tokens=100)
    
    # Check sequence properties
    valid = encoder.validate_sequence(sequence)
    info_density = encoder.get_information_density(sequence)
    
    # Print results
    print(f"Generated sequence of length {len(sequence)}")
    print(f"First 30 nucleotides: {sequence[:30]}")
    print(f"Sequence valid: {valid}")
    print(f"Information density: {info_density:.3f} bits/nt")
    
    # Test GC content
    gc_count = sum(1 for c in sequence if c in 'GC')
    gc_ratio = gc_count / len(sequence)
    
    print(f"GC content: {gc_ratio:.3f}")
    print(f"GC range: {config.gc_min:.3f} - {config.gc_max:.3f}")
    
    # Check homopolymer runs
    max_run = 1
    current_run = 1
    prev_nt = sequence[0]
    
    for nt in sequence[1:]:
        if nt == prev_nt:
            current_run += 1
            max_run = max(max_run, current_run)
        else:
            current_run = 1
        prev_nt = nt
    
    print(f"Maximum homopolymer run: {max_run}")
    print(f"Maximum allowed: {config.max_homopolymer}")
    
    # Verify fix_sequence works
    bad_sequence = "A" * 20 + "C" * 20 + "G" * 20 + "T" * 20
    print(f"\nBad sequence: {bad_sequence}")
    
    fixed = encoder.fix_sequence(bad_sequence)
    print(f"Fixed sequence: {fixed[:30]}...")
    print(f"Fixed sequence valid: {encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)}")
    
    return {
        "sequence_length": len(sequence),
        "is_valid": valid,
        "info_density": info_density,
        "gc_ratio": gc_ratio,
        "max_homopolymer_run": max_run,
        "fixed_sequence_valid": encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)
    }

test_results = test_sequence_generation()
print(f"Test results: {test_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Mock Evo2 integration problems
  - Verify mock implementation returns correct data types
  - Add extensive logging to track method calls
  - Implement caching to improve performance

- **Issue**: HEDGES encoding issues
  - Debug hash computation with sample values
  - Trace bit conversions step by step
  - Verify salt and index generation

### 2.4 Harmonic Module Testing

Test the harmonic processing units with:

```python
import torch
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import LiquidODE, HarmonicFunction, HarmonicProcessingUnit, HPULayer

def test_liquid_neural_dynamics():
    # Test LiquidODE
    state_size = 16
    batch_size = 8
    liquid = LiquidODE(state_size=state_size, hidden_size=state_size*2)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, state_size)
    
    # Test forward pass
    h, y = liquid(x)
    
    print(f"LiquidODE test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Hidden state shape: {h.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    print(f"  Output range: [{y.min().item():.3f}, {y.max().item():.3f}]")
    
    # Test multiple time steps
    h_states = []
    h_current = None
    
    for t in range(10):
        h_current, y_current = liquid(x, h_current, dt=0.05)
        h_states.append(h_current.detach().cpu())
    
    h_trajectory = torch.stack(h_states, dim=0)  # [time, batch, hidden]
    
    print(f"  Multi-step trajectory shape: {h_trajectory.shape}")
    
    # Check if dynamics are changing (not stuck or exploding)
    h_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(h_trajectory[1:] - h_trajectory[:-1]))
    print(f"  Average state change per step: {h_diff.item():.5f}")
    
    if h_diff.item() < 1e-6:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics appear to be stuck (minimal state change)")
    elif h_diff.item() > 10.0:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics may be unstable (large state changes)")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "hidden_shape": h.shape,
        "avg_state_change": h_diff.item()
    }

def test_harmonic_processing_unit():
    # Test HPU
    dim = 16
    batch_size = 8
    hpu = HarmonicProcessingUnit(dim=dim)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, dim)
    
    # Test forward pass
    y = hpu(x)
    
    print(f"\nHPU test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    
    # Test quantum collapse behavior
    outputs = []
    
    for t in range(50):  # Should see collapse around 40Hz (~25ms)
        out = hpu(x, t=t*0.001, dt=0.001)
        outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
    
    outputs = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)  # [time, batch, dim]
    
    # Calculate temporal variations to detect collapse events
    output_diff = torch.abs(outputs[1:] - outputs[:-1])
    max_changes = torch.max(output_diff, dim=2)[0].mean(dim=1)
    
    # Collapse events should show as spikes in the derivative
    collapse_threshold = 0.1
    potential_collapses = torch.where(max_changes > collapse_threshold)[0]
    
    print(f"  Potential collapse events at time steps: {potential_collapses.tolist()}")
    print(f"  Expected collapse frequency: {hpu.or_frequency:.1f} Hz")
    print(f"  Expected collapses in this window: {50 * 0.001 * hpu.or_frequency:.1f}")
    
    # Check bioelectric component
    voltage_magnitude = torch.norm(hpu.voltage).item()
    print(f"  Voltage magnitude: {voltage_magnitude:.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "num_potential_collapses": len(potential_collapses),
        "voltage_magnitude": voltage_magnitude
    }

liquid_results = test_liquid_neural_dynamics()
hpu_results = test_harmonic_processing_unit()

print(f"\nLiquid neural dynamics test results: {liquid_results}")
print(f"HPU test results: {hpu_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Unstable dynamics in LiquidODE
  - Reduce initial weight scales (try 0.01, 0.001)
  - Add gradient clipping during training
  - Implement normalization of states

- **Issue**: Complex arithmetic errors
  - Check for NaN/Inf values in complex tensors
  - Verify complex tensor operations (avoid in-place operations)
  - Add small epsilon values to denominators

- **Issue**: Quantum collapse not occurring
  - Verify collapse threshold calculation
  - Check time tracking and accumulation
  - Trace probability calculations

### 2.5 Digital Cell Testing

Test the digital cell implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import DigitalCell

def test_digital_cell():
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=32, num_cells=1)
    
    # Create digital cell
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0)
    
    # Test input
    batch_size = 4
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs, metrics = cell(inputs)
    
    print(f"Digital cell test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {outputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics: {metrics}")
    
    # Test multiple time steps
    all_outputs = []
    all_metrics = []
    
    for t in range(10):
        out, met = cell(inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        all_outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
        all_metrics.append(met)
    
    # Check growth state progression
    growth_progression = [m['growth'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Growth state progression: {growth_progression}")
    
    # Check energy state
    energy_progression = [m['energy'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Energy progression: {energy_progression}")
    
    # Test cell division if growth is sufficient
    can_divide = cell.should_divide()
    print(f"  Cell ready to divide: {can_divide}")
    
    if can_divide:
        daughter = cell.divide()
        print(f"  Daughter cell created with ID: {daughter.cell_id}")
        
        # Verify daughter properties
        print(f"  Parent energy: {cell.energy.item():.3f}")
        print(f"  Daughter energy: {daughter.energy.item():.3f}")
        print(f"  Parent growth reset: {cell.growth_state.item():.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": outputs.shape,
        "metrics": metrics,
        "growth_progression": growth_progression,
        "energy_progression": energy_progression,
        "can_divide": can_divide
    }

cell_results = test_digital_cell()
print(f"\nDigital cell test results: {cell_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Organelle initialization failures
  - Implement fallback mechanism for each organelle
  - Add detailed error messages for each organelle type
  - Check dimension compatibility between organelles

- **Issue**: Cell state not updating properly
  - Verify state tensor shape and dimensions
  - Check for in-place operations that might not be tracked
  - Add state normalization to prevent drift

- **Issue**: Cell division not working
  - Trace growth state updates
  - Verify division threshold compared to growth state
  - Debug energy distribution during division

### 2.6 Graph Structure Testing

Test the graph structure with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import CellularTissue
import networkx as nx
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def test_cellular_tissue():
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=32, num_cells=10)
    
    # Create tissue
    tissue = CellularTissue(config, initial_cells=8, sparsity=0.3)
    
    # Examine graph properties
    print(f"Cellular tissue test:")
    print(f"  Number of cells: {len(tissue.cells)}")
    print(f"  Number of graph nodes: {tissue.graph.number_of_nodes()}")
    print(f"  Number of graph edges: {tissue.graph.number_of_edges()}")
    
    # Calculate graph metrics
    avg_degree = sum(dict(tissue.graph.degree()).values()) / tissue.graph.number_of_nodes()
    print(f"  Average node degree: {avg_degree:.2f}")
    
    # Check graph is connected
    is_connected = nx.is_connected(tissue.graph)
    print(f"  Graph is connected: {is_connected}")
    
    if not is_connected:
        components = list(nx.connected_components(tissue.graph))
        print(f"  Number of connected components: {len(components)}")
        print(f"  Component sizes: {[len(c) for c in components]}")
    
    # Test forward pass
    batch_size = 4
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, len(tissue.cells), config.d_model)
    
    outputs, metrics = tissue(inputs)
    
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {outputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics: {metrics}")
    
    # Visualize graph structure
    plt.figure(figsize=(8, 6))
    pos = nx.spring_layout(tissue.graph)
    nx.draw(tissue.graph, pos, node_size=500, node_color='lightblue', 
            with_labels=True, font_weight='bold')

with_labels=True, font_weight='bold')
    edge_weights = nx.get_edge_attributes(tissue.graph, 'weight')
    nx.draw_networkx_edge_labels(tissue.graph, pos, edge_labels=edge_weights)
    plt.title("Cellular Tissue Graph Structure")
    plt.savefig("tissue_graph.png")
    plt.close()
    
    return {
        "num_cells": len(tissue.cells),
        "num_edges": tissue.graph.number_of_edges(),
        "avg_degree": avg_degree,
        "is_connected": is_connected,
        "output_shape": outputs.shape,
        "metrics": metrics
    }

tissue_results = test_cellular_tissue()
print(f"\nCellular tissue test results: {tissue_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Graph connectivity problems
  - Verify node indices match cell indices
  - Check edge creation logic in initialization
  - Test with different sparsity values

- **Issue**: Adjacency matrix inconsistent with graph structure
  - Manually compare graph edges with adjacency tensor
  - Verify adjacency updates after graph changes
  - Check tensor device placement

- **Issue**: Cell communication failures
  - Trace message passing through neighbor connections
  - Verify adjacency weights are applied correctly
  - Debug tensor shapes during communication

### 2.7 Neural Controller Testing

Test the neural controller implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController, StripedHyenaAttention

def test_neural_controller():
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=128, num_heads=8, num_layers=4)
    
    # Create controller
    controller = NeuralController(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads,
        num_layers=config.num_layers,
        use_hyena=True  # Test with Striped Hyena Attention
    )
    
    # Test input
    batch_size = 4
    seq_len = 16
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, seq_len, config.d_model)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs = controller(inputs)
    
    print(f"Neural controller test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    
    # Check output dictionary keys
    print(f"  Output keys: {list(outputs.keys())}")
    
    # Check action probabilities
    action_probs = outputs["action_probs"]
    print(f"  Action probabilities shape: {action_probs.shape}")
    print(f"  Action probability sum: {action_probs.sum(dim=1)}")  # Should be close to 1.0
    
    # Test StripedHyena specifically
    hyena = StripedHyenaAttention(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads
    )
    
    hyena_out = hyena(inputs)
    
    print(f"\nStriped Hyena Attention test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {hyena_out.shape}")
    
    # Test long-range dependencies
    # Create input with long-range pattern
    long_seq = 128
    long_input = torch.zeros(1, long_seq, config.d_model)
    
    # Add signal at beginning and end
    long_input[0, 0] = 1.0
    long_input[0, -1] = 1.0
    
    hyena_long_out = hyena(long_input)
    
    # Check if end has influence from beginning (long-range dependency)
    beginning_end_similarity = F.cosine_similarity(
        hyena_long_out[0, 0], hyena_long_out[0, -1], dim=0
    )
    
    print(f"  Long sequence shape: {long_input.shape}")
    print(f"  Beginning-end similarity: {beginning_end_similarity.item():.4f}")
    print(f"  Higher similarity indicates better long-range dependency modeling")
    
    return {
        "action_probs_shape": action_probs.shape,
        "action_prob_sum": action_probs.sum(dim=1).mean().item(),
        "hyena_output_shape": hyena_out.shape,
        "long_range_similarity": beginning_end_similarity.item()
    }

controller_results = test_neural_controller()
print(f"\nNeural controller test results: {controller_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Attention mechanism errors
  - Check for correct masking in self-attention
  - Verify key/query/value projections
  - Debug softmax numerical stability

- **Issue**: Transformer layer normalization problems
  - Verify layer norm implementation with complex tensors
  - Check for NaN values in normalization stats
  - Implement safe normalization with epsilon

- **Issue**: Action head producing invalid probabilities
  - Verify softmax is applied correctly
  - Check for NaN values in logits
  - Debug gradient flow through action head

### 2.8 Self-Organized Criticality Testing

Test the Self-Organized Criticality implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.models.graph_evolution_module import SelfOrganizedCriticality
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

def test_self_organized_criticality():
    # Create SOC model
    soc = SelfOrganizedCriticality(grid_size=32, target_exponent=1.5)
    
    print(f"Self-Organized Criticality test:")
    print(f"  Grid size: {soc.grid_size}x{soc.grid_size}")
    print(f"  Target exponent: {soc.target_exponent}")
    
    # Run system for multiple steps
    energy_means = []
    active_sites = []
    num_steps = 1000
    
    for i in range(num_steps):
        energy, metrics = soc.step()
        
        energy_means.append(metrics["mean_energy"])
        active_sites.append(metrics["num_active_sites"])
        
        if i % 200 == 0:
            print(f"  Step {i}: Mean energy = {metrics['mean_energy']:.4f}, "
                  f"Active sites = {metrics['num_active_sites']}")
    
    # Plot energy evolution
    plt.figure(figsize=(12, 4))
    
    plt.subplot(1, 2, 1)
    plt.plot(energy_means)
    plt.title("Mean Energy Evolution")
    plt.xlabel("Time Step")
    plt.ylabel("Mean Energy")
    
    plt.subplot(1, 2, 2)
    plt.plot(active_sites)
    plt.title("Active Sites Evolution")
    plt.xlabel("Time Step")
    plt.ylabel("Number of Active Sites")
    
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.savefig("soc_evolution.png")
    plt.close()
    
    # Get avalanche distribution
    bin_centers, counts = soc.get_avalanche_distribution()
    
    # Check if we have enough avalanche data
    if len(bin_centers) > 0:
        # Plot avalanche distribution
        plt.figure(figsize=(8, 6))
        plt.loglog(bin_centers, counts, 'o-')
        
        # Fit power law
        if len(bin_centers) > 2:
            # Simple linear fit in log-log space
            log_x = np.log(bin_centers)
            log_y = np.log(counts)
            
            # Fit line
            coeffs = np.polyfit(log_x, log_y, 1)
            exponent = -coeffs[0]  # Negative slope is the exponent
            
            # Plot fit
            fit_y = np.exp(coeffs[1]) * bin_centers ** (-exponent)
            plt.loglog(bin_centers, fit_y, 'r--', 
                      label=f'Power law: $\\tau$ = {exponent:.2f}')
            plt.legend()
        
        plt.title("Avalanche Size Distribution")
        plt.xlabel("Avalanche Size")
        plt.ylabel("Probability")
        plt.savefig("avalanche_distribution.png")
        plt.close()
        
        print(f"  Avalanche analysis:")
        print(f"  Number of recorded avalanches: {len(soc.avalanche_sizes)}")
        print(f"  Fitted power law exponent: {exponent:.2f}")
        print(f"  Target exponent: {soc.target_exponent}")
    else:
        print(f"  Not enough avalanches recorded for distribution analysis")
    
    # Check final metrics
    final_energy, final_metrics = soc.step()
    print(f"  Final metrics: {final_metrics}")
    
    return {
        "num_steps": num_steps,
        "final_mean_energy": final_metrics["mean_energy"],
        "num_avalanches": len(soc.avalanche_sizes),
        "fitted_exponent": exponent if len(bin_centers) > 2 else None,
        "target_exponent": soc.target_exponent
    }

soc_results = test_self_organized_criticality()
print(f"\nSOC test results: {soc_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Avalanche distributions not following power law
  - Adjust driving rate and threshold parameters
  - Increase number of iterations for better statistics
  - Check boundary conditions in grid implementation

- **Issue**: System not reaching critical state
  - Verify energy addition and dissipation balance
  - Check toppling rules for energy redistribution
  - Debug threshold mechanism and site activity

- **Issue**: NaN or infinite values
  - Add bounds checking for energy values
  - Implement clipping for extreme values
  - Add safety checks in avalanche exponent calculation

## 3. Integration Testing

### 3.1 Component Integration

Test integration of components with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import HPULayer
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import DigitalCell, CellularTissue, OrganismLayer
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController

def test_component_integration():
    # Create configuration
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=64,
        num_cells=16,
        num_layers=4,
        num_heads=4,
        bioelectric_kappa=0.1,
        or_frequency=40.0
    )
    
    print(f"Component integration test:")
    
    # Initialize DNA encoder
    dna_encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    print(f"  DNA encoder initialized")
    
    # Generate DNA sequence for cell
    dna_sequence = dna_encoder.generate_sequence("Test cell architecture", n_tokens=100)
    print(f"  Generated DNA sequence of length {len(dna_sequence)}")
    
    # Create digital cell with DNA
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0, dna_sequence=dna_sequence)
    print(f"  Digital cell created with DNA")
    
    # Create tissue with multiple cells
    tissue = CellularTissue(config, initial_cells=8, dna_encoder=dna_encoder)
    print(f"  Cellular tissue created with {len(tissue.cells)} cells")
    
    # Create organism layer
    organism = OrganismLayer(
        config, 
        num_tissues=2, 
        cells_per_tissue=8, 
        dna_encoder=dna_encoder
    )
    print(f"  Organism layer created with {organism.num_tissues} tissues")
    
    # Create neural controller
    controller = NeuralController(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads,
        num_layers=config.num_layers
    )
    print(f"  Neural controller created")
    
    # Test data flow: Controller -> Organism -> Tissue -> Cell
    batch_size = 2
    
    # Create input for controller
    controller_input = torch.randn(batch_size, 10, config.d_model)
    controller_output = controller(controller_input)
    print(f"  Controller output keys: {list(controller_output.keys())}")
    
    # Create input for organism
    organism_input = torch.randn(batch_size, organism.num_tissues, 8, config.d_model)
    organism_output, organism_metrics = organism(organism_input)
    print(f"  Organism output shape: {organism_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Organism metrics: {organism_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for tissue
    tissue_input = torch.randn(batch_size, len(tissue.cells), config.d_model)
    tissue_output, tissue_metrics = tissue(tissue_input)
    print(f"  Tissue output shape: {tissue_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Tissue metrics: {tissue_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for cell
    cell_input = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    cell_output, cell_metrics = cell(cell_input)
    print(f"  Cell output shape: {cell_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Cell metrics: {cell_metrics}")
    
    return {
        "controller_output_keys": list(controller_output.keys()),
        "organism_output_shape": list(organism_output.shape),
        "tissue_output_shape": list(tissue_output.shape),
        "cell_output_shape": list(cell_output.shape)
    }

integration_results = test_component_integration()
print(f"\nComponent integration test results: {integration_results}")
```

### 3.2 Full Model Integration

Implement the full model integration with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import HPULayer
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import OrganismLayer
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController
from lhllm.models.graph_evolution_module import SelfOrganizedCriticality, ReactionSystem

class LHLLM(nn.Module):
    """Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model."""
    
    def __init__(self, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.config = config
        
        # Create DNA encoder
        self.dna_encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
        
        # Create organism layer
        self.organism = OrganismLayer(
            config,
            num_tissues=4,
            cells_per_tissue=16,
            dna_encoder=self.dna_encoder
        )
        
        # Create neural controller
        self.controller = NeuralController(
            d_model=config.d_model,
            num_heads=config.num_heads,
            num_layers=config.num_layers
        )
        
        # Create self-organized criticality system
        self.soc = SelfOrganizedCriticality(
            grid_size=32,
            target_exponent=config.target_values["avalanche_exponent"]
        )
        
        # Create reaction system
        self.reaction_system = ReactionSystem(
            num_reactants=16,
            num_reactions=32,
            complex_valued=config.fp_precision == "complex64"
        )
        
        # Output projection
        self.output_projection = nn.Linear(config.d_model, config.d_model)
    
    def forward(self, inputs, t=0.0, dt=0.01):
        batch_size = inputs.shape[0]
        
        # Process through neural controller
        controller_output = self.controller(inputs)
        
        # Extract action probabilities
        action_probs = controller_output["action_probs"]
        
        # Create organism input from controller output
        # Reshape to match organism input shape [batch, num_tissues, cells_per_tissue, d_model]
        organism_input = inputs.unsqueeze(1).unsqueeze(1).expand(
            batch_size, 
            self.organism.num_tissues,
            self.organism.tissues[0].cells_count,
            self.config.d_model
        )
        
        # Process through organism
        organism_output, organism_metrics = self.organism(organism_input, dt)
        
        # Update SOC system
        soc_energy, soc_metrics = self.soc.step()
        
        # Update reaction system
        reactions, reaction_metrics = self.reaction_system.step(dt, organism_output)
        
        # Apply output projection
        output = self.output_projection(organism_output)
        
        # Combine metrics
        metrics = {
            **controller_output,
            **organism_metrics,
            **soc_metrics,
            **reaction_metrics
        }
        
        return output, metrics

def test_full_model():
    # Create configuration
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=128,
        num_cells=16,
        num_layers=4,
        num_heads=4
    )
    
    # Create model
    model = LHLLM(config)
    print(f"Full model created")
    
    # Test forward pass
    batch_size = 2
    seq_len = 10
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, seq_len, config.d_model)
    
    output, metrics = model(inputs)
    
    print(f"Full model test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {output.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics keys: {list(metrics.keys())}")
    
    # Test stateful behavior
    outputs = []
    for t in range(10):
        out, _ = model(inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
    
    # Check consistency and evolution
    outputs = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)  # [time, batch, d_model]
    output_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(outputs[1:] - outputs[:-1]))
    
    print(f"  Output evolution over time:")
    print(f"    Average change between steps: {output_diff.item():.6f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": list(output.shape),
        "metrics_keys": list(metrics.keys()),
        "avg_step_change": output_diff.item()
    }

model_results = test_full_model()
print(f"\nFull model test results: {model_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**

  - Reduce model size for testing
  - Use mixed precision (FP16) training

- **Issue**: Forward pass fails with shape mismatch
  - Add shape checking between component boundaries
  - Debug tensor reshaping operations
  - Trace inputs through each component

### 3.3 Memory Profiling

Profile the model's memory usage with:

```python
import torch
import gc
import psutil
import os

def profile_memory(model_cls, config, input_shapes, num_iterations=5):
    # Force garbage collection
    gc.collect()
    torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    # Get initial memory usage
    process = psutil.Process(os.getpid())
    initial_cpu_memory = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        initial_gpu_memory = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        initial_gpu_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        initial_gpu_memory = 0
        initial_gpu_cached = 0
    
    print(f"Initial memory usage:")
    print(f"  CPU: {initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB")
    
    # Create model
    model = model_cls(config)
    model.to(config.device)
    
    # Get memory after model creation
    post_model_cpu = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        post_model_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        post_model_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        post_model_gpu = 0
        post_model_cached = 0
    
    print(f"After model creation:")
    print(f"  CPU: {post_model_cpu:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_cpu - initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {post_model_gpu:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_gpu - initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {post_model_cached:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_cached - initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB)")
    
    # Create inputs
    inputs = []
    for shape in input_shapes:
        inputs.append(torch.randn(*shape, device=config.device))
    
    # Track forward pass memory
    max_memory = post_model_gpu
    
    # Run multiple iterations
    for i in range(num_iterations):
        # Forward pass
        with torch.no_grad():
            outputs = model(*inputs)
        
        # Get memory usage
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            current_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
            max_memory = max(max_memory, current_gpu)
        
        # Force garbage collection between iterations
        gc.collect()
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    # Final memory usage
    final_cpu = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        final_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        final_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        final_gpu = 0
        final_cached = 0
    
    print(f"After {num_iterations} iterations:")
    print(f"  CPU: {final_cpu:.2f} MB (+ {final_cpu - initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {final_gpu:.2f} MB (+ {final_gpu - initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {final_cached:.2f} MB (+ {final_cached - initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  Max GPU memory: {max_memory:.2f} MB")
    
    # Clean up
    del model
    del inputs
    gc.collect()
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    return {
        "initial_cpu_memory": initial_cpu_memory,
        "initial_gpu_memory": initial_gpu_memory,
        "model_cpu_memory": post_model_cpu - initial_cpu_memory,
        "model_gpu_memory": post_model_gpu - initial_gpu_memory,
        "final_cpu_memory": final_cpu - initial_cpu_memory,
        "final_gpu_memory": final_gpu - initial_gpu_memory,
        "max_gpu_memory": max_memory
    }

# Profile the LHLLM model
config = LHLLMConfig(
    d_model=128,
    num_cells=16,
    num_layers=4,
    num_heads=4
)

# Define input shapes
input_shapes = [(2, 10, config.d_model)]

memory_profile = profile_memory(LHLLM, config, input_shapes)
print(f"\nMemory profile: {memory_profile}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Excessive memory usage
  - Implement incremental component initialization
  - Use parameter sharing between components
  - Add hooks to track tensor allocations

- **Issue**: Memory leaks
  - Check for circular references
  - Monitor tensor references with weak references
  - Debug buffer registrations

## 4. Training Pipeline

### 4.1 Diffusion Evolution Implementation

Implement diffusion evolution optimization with:

```python
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
import numpy as np
from typing import Callable, List, Tuple

class DiffusionEvolution:
    """Parameter optimization using latent space diffusion."""
    
    def __init__(self, 
                latent_dim: int, 
                param_dim: int,
                num_steps: int = 50,
                beta_schedule: str = 'linear',
                min_beta: float = 0.1,
                max_beta: float = 0.9,
                device: str = 'cuda'):
        """
        Initialize a Diffusion Evolution optimizer.
        """
        self.latent_dim = latent_dim
        self.param_dim = param_dim
        self.num_steps = num_steps
        self.device = device
        
        # Create beta schedule
        if beta_schedule == 'linear':
            self.betas = torch.linspace(min_beta, max_beta, num_steps)
        elif beta_schedule == 'cosine':
            self.betas = torch.cos(torch.linspace(0, np.pi/2, num_steps)) * (max_beta - min_beta) + min_beta
        elif beta_schedule == 'quadratic':
            self.betas = torch.linspace(min_beta**0.5, max_beta**0.5, num_steps) ** 2
        else:
            raise ValueError(f"Unsupported beta schedule: {beta_schedule}")
        
        self.betas = self.betas.to(device)
        
        # Precompute diffusion parameters
        self.alphas = 1.0 - self.betas
        self.alphas_cumprod = torch.cumprod(self.alphas, dim=0)
        self.alphas_cumprod_prev = F.pad(self.alphas_cumprod[:-1], (1, 0), value=1.0)
        self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod = torch.sqrt(self.alphas_cumprod)
        self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod = torch.sqrt(1.0 - self.alphas_cumprod)
        
        # Create encoder and decoder networks
        self.encoder = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(param_dim, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        self.decoder = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(latent_dim, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, param_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        # Create denoiser network
        self.denoiser = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(latent_dim + 1, latent_dim * 2),  # +1 for time step embedding
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        # Optimizer for training the networks
        self.optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(
            list(self.encoder.parameters()) + 
            list(self.decoder.parameters()) + 
            list(self.denoiser.parameters()),
            lr=1e-4
        )
    
    def train_step(self, params_batch: torch.Tensor) -> float:
        """
        Train the diffusion model on a batch of parameters.
        
        Args:
            params_batch: Parameter batch [batch_size, param_dim]
            
        Returns:
            Loss value
        """
        batch_size = params_batch.shape[0]
        
        # Move to device
        params_batch = params_batch.to(self.device)
        
        # Encode parameters
        z = self.encoder(params_batch)
        
        # Choose random timesteps
        t = torch.randint(0, self.num_steps, (batch_size,), device=self.device)
        
        # Add noise according to the timestep
        noise = torch.randn_like(z)
        sqrt_alphas = self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        sqrt_one_minus_alphas = self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        
        noisy_z = sqrt_alphas * z + sqrt_one_minus_alphas * noise
        
        # Time embedding
        t_embed = t.float().view(-1, 1) / self.num_steps
        
        # Predict noise
        noise_pred = self.denoiser(torch.cat([noisy_z, t_embed], dim=1))
        
        # Loss: MSE between predicted and actual noise
        loss = F.mse_loss(noise_pred, noise)
        
        # Backward pass
        self.optimizer.zero_grad()
        loss.backward()
        self.optimizer.step()
        
        return loss.item()
    
    def diffuse(self, z: torch.Tensor, t: int) -> Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor]:
        """
        Apply diffusion for a specific time step.
        
        Args:
            z: Latent tensor
            t: Time step
            
        Returns:
            Tuple of (noisy latent, noise)
        """
        noise = torch.randn_like(z)
        sqrt_alphas_cumprod_t = self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod_t = self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        
        noisy_z = sqrt_alphas_cumprod_t * z + sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod_t * noise
        return noisy_z, noise
    
    def denoise_step(self, noisy_z: torch.Tensor, t: int) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Perform a single denoising step.
        
        Args:
            noisy_z: Noisy latent tensor
            t: Time step
            
        Returns:
            Denoised latent tensor
        """
        # Create time embedding
        t_embed = torch.ones(noisy_z.shape[0], 1, device=self.device) * t / self.num_steps
        
        # Predict noise
        predicted_noise = self.denoiser(torch.cat([noisy_z, t_"""
This document provides a comprehensive development and debugging guide for implementing
the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM). It contains detailed instructions and 
debugging tips for each component.
"""

### 1.4 CUDA Verification

```python
import torch

def verify_cuda():
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        print(f"CUDA is available")
        print(f"Current CUDA device: {torch.cuda.current_device()}")
        print(f"CUDA device name: {torch.cuda.get_device_name(0)}")
        print(f"CUDA device count: {torch.cuda.device_count()}")
        
        # Test CUDA operation
        x = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        y = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        z = torch.matmul(x, y)
        print(f"CUDA operation successful. Result shape: {z.shape}")
        
        # Test complex tensor support
        complex_tensor = torch.complex(torch.rand(10, 10).cuda(), torch.rand(10, 10).cuda())
        print(f"Complex tensor on CUDA created. Shape: {complex_tensor.shape}")
        
        return True
    else:
        print("CUDA is not available")
        return False

verify_cuda()
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: CUDA shows available but operations fail
  - Restart kernel/Python interpreter
  - Check for CUDA out-of-memory errors
  - Verify CUDA driver and toolkit compatibility

- **Issue**: Complex tensors not supported
  - Ensure PyTorch version >= 1.9 for complex tensor support
  - Fallback to real tensors and manual complex arithmetic if needed

### 2.3 DNA Module Testing

Test the DNA module implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder

def test_sequence_generation():
    config = LHLLMConfig()
    encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    
    # Generate sequence
    sequence = encoder.generate_sequence("Test prompt", n_tokens=100)
    
    # Check sequence properties
    valid = encoder.validate_sequence(sequence)
    info_density = encoder.get_information_density(sequence)
    
    # Print results
    print(f"Generated sequence of length {len(sequence)}")
    print(f"First 30 nucleotides: {sequence[:30]}")
    print(f"Sequence valid: {valid}")
    print(f"Information density: {info_density:.3f} bits/nt")
    
    # Test GC content
    gc_count = sum(1 for c in sequence if c in 'GC')
    gc_ratio = gc_count / len(sequence)
    
    print(f"GC content: {gc_ratio:.3f}")
    print(f"GC range: {config.gc_min:.3f} - {config.gc_max:.3f}")
    
    # Check homopolymer runs
    max_run = 1
    current_run = 1
    prev_nt = sequence[0]
    
    for nt in sequence[1:]:
        if nt == prev_nt:
            current_run += 1
            max_run = max(max_run, current_run)
        else:
            current_run = 1
        prev_nt = nt
    
    print(f"Maximum homopolymer run: {max_run}")
    print(f"Maximum allowed: {config.max_homopolymer}")
    
    # Verify fix_sequence works
    bad_sequence = "A" * 20 + "C" * 20 + "G" * 20 + "T" * 20
    print(f"\nBad sequence: {bad_sequence}")
    
    fixed = encoder.fix_sequence(bad_sequence)
    print(f"Fixed sequence: {fixed[:30]}...")
    print(f"Fixed sequence valid: {encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)}")
    
    return {
        "sequence_length": len(sequence),
        "is_valid": valid,
        "info_density": info_density,
        "gc_ratio": gc_ratio,
        "max_homopolymer_run": max_run,
        "fixed_sequence_valid": encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)
    }

test_results = test_sequence_generation()
print(f"Test results: {test_results}")
```

### 2.4 Harmonic Module Testing

Test the harmonic processing units with:

```python
import torch
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import LiquidODE, HarmonicFunction, HarmonicProcessingUnit, HPULayer

def test_liquid_neural_dynamics():
    # Test LiquidODE
    state_size = 16
    batch_size = 8
    liquid = LiquidODE(state_size=state_size, hidden_size=state_size*2)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, state_size)
    
    # Test forward pass
    h, y = liquid(x)
    
    print(f"LiquidODE test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Hidden state shape: {h.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    print(f"  Output range: [{y.min().item():.3f}, {y.max().item():.3f}]")
    
    # Test multiple time steps
    h_states = []
    h_current = None
    
    for t in range(10):
        h_current, y_current = liquid(x, h_current, dt=0.05)
        h_states.append(h_current.detach().cpu())
    
    h_trajectory = torch.stack(h_states, dim=0)  # [time, batch, hidden]
    
    print(f"  Multi-step trajectory shape: {h_trajectory.shape}")
    
    # Check if dynamics are changing (not stuck or exploding)
    h_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(h_trajectory[1:] - h_trajectory[:-1]))
    print(f"  Average state change per step: {h_diff.item():.5f}")
    
    if h_diff.item() < 1e-6:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics appear to be stuck (minimal state change)")
    elif h_diff.item() > 10.0:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics may be unstable (large state changes)")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "hidden_shape": h.shape,
        "avg_state_change": h_diff.item()
    }

def test_harmonic_processing_unit():
    # Test HPU
    dim = 16
    batch_size = 8
    hpu = HarmonicProcessingUnit(dim=dim)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, dim)
    
    # Test forward pass
    y = hpu(x)
    
    print(f"\nHPU test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    
    # Test quantum collapse behavior
    outputs = []
    
    for t in range(50):  # Should see collapse around 40Hz (~25ms)
        out = hpu(x, t=t*0.001, dt=0.001)
        outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
    
    outputs = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)  # [time, batch, dim]
    
    # Calculate temporal variations to detect collapse events
    output_diff = torch.abs(outputs[1:] - outputs[:-1])
    max_changes = torch.max(output_diff, dim=2)[0].mean(dim=1)
    
    # Collapse events should show as spikes in the derivative
    collapse_threshold = 0.1
    potential_collapses = torch.where(max_changes > collapse_threshold)[0]
    
    print(f"  Potential collapse events at time steps: {potential_collapses.tolist()}")
    print(f"  Expected collapse frequency: {hpu.or_frequency:.1f} Hz")
    print(f"  Expected collapses in this window: {50 * 0.001 * hpu.or_frequency:.1f}")
    
    # Check bioelectric component
    voltage_magnitude = torch.norm(hpu.voltage).item()
    print(f"  Voltage magnitude: {voltage_magnitude:.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "num_potential_collapses": len(potential_collapses),
        "voltage_magnitude": voltage_magnitude
    }

liquid_results = test_liquid_neural_dynamics()
hpu_results = test_harmonic_processing_unit()

print(f"\nLiquid neural dynamics test results: {liquid_results}")
print(f"HPU test results: {hpu_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Unstable dynamics in LiquidODE
  - Reduce initial weight scales (try 0.01, 0.001)
  - Add gradient clipping during training
  - Implement normalization of states

- **Issue**: Complex arithmetic errors
  - Check for NaN/Inf values in complex tensors
  - Verify complex tensor operations (avoid in-place operations)
  - Add small epsilon values to denominators

- **Issue**: Quantum collapse not occurring
  - Verify collapse threshold calculation
  - Check time tracking and accumulation
  - Trace probability calculations

    # Create digital cell
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0)

    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs, metrics = cell(inputs)
    
    print(f"Digital cell test:")

    print(f"  Output shape: {outputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics: {metrics}")

    all_outputs = []
    all_metrics = []
    
    for t in range(10):
        out, met = cell(inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        all_outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
        all_metrics.append(met)
    
    # Check growth state progression
    growth_progression = [m['growth'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Growth state progression: {growth_progression}")
    
    # Check energy state
    energy_progression = [m['energy'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Energy progression: {energy_progression}")
    
    # Test cell division if growth is sufficient

        print(f"  Parent energy: {cell.energy.item():.3f}")

        print(f"  Parent growth reset: {cell.growth_state.item():.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": outputs.shape,
        "metrics": metrics,
        "growth_progression": growth_progression,
        "energy_progression": energy_progression,
        "can_divide": can_divide
    }
