Test integration of components with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import HPULayer
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import DigitalCell, CellularTissue, OrganismLayer
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController

def test_component_integration():
    # Create configuration
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=64,
        num_cells=16,
        num_layers=4,
        num_heads=4,
        bioelectric_kappa=0.1,
        or_frequency=40.0
    )
    
    print(f"Component integration test:")
    
    # Initialize DNA encoder
    dna_encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    print(f"  DNA encoder initialized")
    
    # Generate DNA sequence for cell
    dna_sequence = dna_encoder.generate_sequence("Test cell architecture", n_tokens=100)
    print(f"  Generated DNA sequence of length {len(dna_sequence)}")
    
    # Create digital cell with DNA
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0, dna_sequence=dna_sequence)
    print(f"  Digital cell created with DNA")

    tissue = CellularTissue(config, initial_cells=8, dna_encoder=dna_encoder)

        dna_encoder=dna_encoder
    )
    print(f"  Organism layer created with {organism.num_tissues} tissues")
    
    # Create neural controller
    controller = NeuralController(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads,
        num_layers=config.num_layers
    )
    print(f"  Neural controller created")
    
    # Test data flow: Controller -> Organism -> Tissue -> Cell
    batch_size = 2
    
    # Create input for controller
    controller_input = torch.randn(batch_size, 10, config.d_model)
    controller_output = controller(controller_input)
    print(f"  Controller output keys: {list(controller_output.keys())}")
    
    # Create input for organism
    organism_input = torch.randn(batch_size, organism.num_tissues, 8, config.d_model)
    organism_output, organism_metrics = organism(organism_input)
    print(f"  Organism output shape: {organism_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Organism metrics: {organism_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for tissue
    tissue_input = torch.randn(batch_size, len(tissue.cells), config.d_model)
    tissue_output, tissue_metrics = tissue(tissue_input)
    print(f"  Tissue output shape: {tissue_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Tissue metrics: {tissue_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for cell
    cell_input = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    cell_output, cell_metrics = cell(cell_input)
    print(f"  Cell output shape: {cell_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Cell metrics: {cell_metrics}")
    
    return {
        "controller_output_keys": list(controller_output.keys()),
        "organism_output_shape": list(organism_output.shape),
        "tissue_output_shape": list(tissue_output.shape),
        "cell_output_shape": list(cell_output.shape)
    }

integration_results = test_component_integration()
print(f"\nComponent integration test results: {integration_results}")

### 3.2 Full Model Integration

Implement the full model integration with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import HPULayer
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import OrganismLayer
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController
from lhllm.models.graph_evolution_module import SelfOrganizedCriticality, ReactionSystem

class LHLLM(nn.Module):
    """Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model."""
    
    def __init__(self, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.config = config
        
        # Create DNA encoder
        self.dna_encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
        
        # Create organism layer
        self.organism = OrganismLayer(
            config,
            num_tissues=4,
            cells_per_tissue=16,
            dna_encoder=self.dna_encoder
        )
        
        # Create neural controller
        self.controller = NeuralController(
            d_model=config.d_model,
            num_heads=config.num_heads,
            num_layers=config.num_layers
        )
        
        # Create self-organized criticality system
        self.soc = SelfOrganizedCriticality(
            grid_size=32,
            target_exponent=config.target_values["avalanche_exponent"]
        )
        
        # Create reaction system
        self.reaction_system = ReactionSystem(
            num_reactants=16,
            num_reactions=32,
            complex_valued=config.fp_precision == "complex64"
        )
        
        # Output projection
        self.output_projection = nn.Linear(config.d_model, config.d_model)
    
    def forward(self, inputs, t=0.0, dt=0.01):
        batch_size = inputs.shape[0]
        
        # Process through neural controller
        controller_output = self.controller(inputs)
        
        # Extract action probabilities
        action_probs = controller_output["action_probs"]
        
        # Create organism input from controller output
        # Reshape to match organism input shape [batch, num_tissues, cells_per_tissue, d_model]
        organism_input = inputs.unsqueeze(1).unsqueeze(1).expand(
            batch_size, 
            self.organism.num_tissues,
            self.organism.tissues[0].cells_count,
            self.config.d_model
        )
        
        # Process through organism
        organism_output, organism_metrics = self.organism(organism_input, dt)
        
        # Update SOC system
        soc_energy, soc_metrics = self.soc.step()
        
        # Update reaction system
        reactions, reaction_metrics = self.reaction_system.step(dt, organism_output)
        
        # Apply output projection
        output = self.output_projection(organism_output)
        
        # Combine metrics
        metrics = {
            **controller_output,
            **organism_metrics,
            **soc_metrics,
            **reaction_metrics
        }
        
        return output, metrics

def test_full_model():
    # Create configuration
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=128,
        num_cells=16,
        num_layers=4,
        num_heads=4
    )
    
    # Create model
    model = LHLLM(config)
    print(f"Full model created")
    
    # Test forward pass
    batch_size = 2
    seq_len = 10
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, seq_len, config.d_model)
    
    output, metrics = model(inputs)
    
    print(f"Full model test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {output.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics keys: {list(metrics.keys())}")
    
    # Test stateful behavior
    outputs = []
    for t in range(10):
        out, _ = model(inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
    
    # Check consistency and evolution
    outputs = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)  # [time, batch, d_model]
    output_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(outputs[1:] - outputs[:-1]))
    
    print(f"  Output evolution over time:")
    print(f"    Average change between steps: {output_diff.item():.6f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": list(output.shape),
        "metrics_keys": list(metrics.keys()),
        "avg_step_change": output_diff.item()
    }

model_results = test_full_model()
print(f"\nFull model test results: {model_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Model complexity overwhelms GPU memory
  - Implement gradient checkpointing
  - Reduce model size for testing
  - Use mixed precision (FP16) training

- **Issue**: Forward pass fails with shape mismatch
  - Add shape checking between component boundaries
  - Debug tensor reshaping operations
  - Trace inputs through each component

### 3.3 Memory Profiling

Profile the model's memory usage with:

```python
import torch
import gc
import psutil
import os

def profile_memory(model_cls, config, input_shapes, num_iterations=5):
    # Force garbage collection
    gc.collect()
    torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    # Get initial memory usage
    process = psutil.Process(os.getpid())
    initial_cpu_memory = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        initial_gpu_memory = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        initial_gpu_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        initial_gpu_memory = 0
        initial_gpu_cached = 0
    
    print(f"Initial memory usage:")
    print(f"  CPU: {initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB")
    
    # Create model
    model = model_cls(config)
    model.to(config.device)
    
    # Get memory after model creation
    post_model_cpu = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        post_model_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        post_model_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        post_model_gpu = 0
        post_model_cached = 0
    
    print(f"After model creation:")
    print(f"  CPU: {post_model_cpu:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_cpu - initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {post_model_gpu:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_gpu - initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {post_model_cached:.2f} MB (+ {post_model_cached - initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB)")
    
    # Create inputs
    inputs = []
    for shape in input_shapes:
        inputs.append(torch.randn(*shape, device=config.device))
    
    # Track forward pass memory
    max_memory = post_model_gpu
    
    # Run multiple iterations
    for i in range(num_iterations):
        # Forward pass
        with torch.no_grad():
            outputs = model(*inputs)
        
        # Get memory usage
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            current_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
            max_memory = max(max_memory, current_gpu)
        
        # Force garbage collection between iterations
        gc.collect()
        if torch.cuda.is_available():
            torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    # Final memory usage
    final_cpu = process.memory_info().rss / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        final_gpu = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
        final_cached = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024 / 1024  # MB
    else:
        final_gpu = 0
        final_cached = 0
    
    print(f"After {num_iterations} iterations:")
    print(f"  CPU: {final_cpu:.2f} MB (+ {final_cpu - initial_cpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU allocated: {final_gpu:.2f} MB (+ {final_gpu - initial_gpu_memory:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  GPU cached: {final_cached:.2f} MB (+ {final_cached - initial_gpu_cached:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"  Max GPU memory: {max_memory:.2f} MB")
    
    # Clean up
    del model
    del inputs
    gc.collect()
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    
    return {
        "initial_cpu_memory": initial_cpu_memory,
        "initial_gpu_memory": initial_gpu_memory,
        "model_cpu_memory": post_model_cpu - initial_cpu_memory,
        "model_gpu_memory": post_model_gpu - initial_gpu_memory,
        "final_cpu_memory": final_cpu - initial_cpu_memory,
        "final_gpu_memory": final_gpu - initial_gpu_memory,
        "max_gpu_memory": max_memory
    }

# Profile the LHLLM model
config = LHLLMConfig(
    d_model=128,
    num_cells=16,
    num_layers=4,
    num_heads=4
)

# Define input shapes
input_shapes = [(2, 10, config.d_model)]

memory_profile = profile_memory(LHLLM, config, input_shapes)
print(f"\nMemory profile: {memory_profile}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Excessive memory usage
  - Implement incremental component initialization
  - Use parameter sharing between components
  - Add hooks to track tensor allocations

- **Issue**: Memory leaks
  - Check for circular references
  - Monitor tensor references with weak references
  - Debug buffer registrations

## 4. Training Pipeline

### 4.1 Diffusion Evolution Implementation

Implement diffusion evolution optimization with:

```python
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
import numpy as np
from typing import Callable, List, Tuple

class DiffusionEvolution:
    """Parameter optimization using latent space diffusion."""
    
    def __init__(self, 
                latent_dim: int, 
                param_dim: int,
                num_steps: int = 50,
                beta_schedule: str = 'linear',
                min_beta: float = 0.1,
                max_beta: float = 0.9,
                device: str = 'cuda'):
        """
        Initialize a Diffusion Evolution optimizer.
        """
        self.latent_dim = latent_dim
        self.param_dim = param_dim
        self.num_steps = num_steps
        self.device = device
        
        # Create beta schedule
        if beta_schedule == 'linear':
            self.betas = torch.linspace(min_beta, max_beta, num_steps)
        elif beta_schedule == 'cosine':
            self.betas = torch.cos(torch.linspace(0, np.pi/2, num_steps)) * (max_beta - min_beta) + min_beta
        elif beta_schedule == 'quadratic':
            self.betas = torch.linspace(min_beta**0.5, max_beta**0.5, num_steps) ** 2
        else:
            raise ValueError(f"Unsupported beta schedule: {beta_schedule}")
        
        self.betas = self.betas.to(device)
        
        # Precompute diffusion parameters
        self.alphas = 1.0 - self.betas
        self.alphas_cumprod = torch.cumprod(self.alphas, dim=0)
        self.alphas_cumprod_prev = F.pad(self.alphas_cumprod[:-1], (1, 0), value=1.0)
        self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod = torch.sqrt(self.alphas_cumprod)
        self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod = torch.sqrt(1.0 - self.alphas_cumprod)
        
        # Create encoder and decoder networks
        self.encoder = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(param_dim, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        self.decoder = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(latent_dim, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, param_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        # Create denoiser network
        self.denoiser = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(latent_dim + 1, latent_dim * 2),  # +1 for time step embedding
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim * 2),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(latent_dim * 2, latent_dim)
        ).to(device)
        
        # Optimizer for training the networks
        self.optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(
            list(self.encoder.parameters()) + 
            list(self.decoder.parameters()) + 
            list(self.denoiser.parameters()),
            lr=1e-4
        )
    
    def train_step(self, params_batch: torch.Tensor) -> float:
        """
        Train the diffusion model on a batch of parameters.
        
        Args:
            params_batch: Parameter batch [batch_size, param_dim]
            
        Returns:
            Loss value
        """
        batch_size = params_batch.shape[0]
        
        # Move to device
        params_batch = params_batch.to(self.device)
        
        # Encode parameters
        z = self.encoder(params_batch)
        
        # Choose random timesteps
        t = torch.randint(0, self.num_steps, (batch_size,), device=self.device)
        
        # Add noise according to the timestep
        noise = torch.randn_like(z)
        sqrt_alphas = self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        sqrt_one_minus_alphas = self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        
        noisy_z = sqrt_alphas * z + sqrt_one_minus_alphas * noise
        
        # Time embedding
        t_embed = t.float().view(-1, 1) / self.num_steps
        
        # Predict noise
        noise_pred = self.denoiser(torch.cat([noisy_z, t_embed], dim=1))
        
        # Loss: MSE between predicted and actual noise
        loss = F.mse_loss(noise_pred, noise)
        
        # Backward pass
        self.optimizer.zero_grad()
        loss.backward()
        self.optimizer.step()
        
        return loss.item()
    
    def diffuse(self, z: torch.Tensor, t: int) -> Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor]:
        """
        Apply diffusion for a specific time step.
        
        Args:
            z: Latent tensor
            t: Time step
            
        Returns:
            Tuple of (noisy latent, noise)
        """
        noise = torch.randn_like(z)
        sqrt_alphas_cumprod_t = self.sqrt_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod_t = self.sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod[t].view(-1, 1)
        
        noisy_z = sqrt_alphas_cumprod_t * z + sqrt_one_minus_alphas_cumprod_t * noise
        return noisy_z, noise
    
    def denoise_step(self, noisy_z: torch.Tensor, t: int) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Perform a single denoising step.
        
        Args:
            noisy_z: Noisy latent tensor
            t: Time step
            
        Returns:
            Denoised latent tensor
        """
        # Create time embedding
        t_embed = torch.ones(noisy_z.shape[0], 1, device=self.device) * t / self.num_steps
        
        # Predict noise
        predicted_noise = self.denoiser(torch.cat([noisy_z, t_"""
This document provides a comprehensive development and debugging guide for implementing
the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM). It contains detailed instructions and 
debugging tips for each component.
"""

  - Verify conda is updated with `conda update -n base -c defaults conda`

**Debugging Tips:**

  - Match PyTorch version accordingly (visit pytorch.org)

  - Check package conflicts with `pip check`
  - Try installing problematic packages separately

```python
import torch

def verify_cuda():
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        print(f"CUDA is available")
        print(f"Current CUDA device: {torch.cuda.current_device()}")
        print(f"CUDA device name: {torch.cuda.get_device_name(0)}")
        print(f"CUDA device count: {torch.cuda.device_count()}")
        
        # Test CUDA operation
        x = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        y = torch.rand(1000, 1000).cuda()
        z = torch.matmul(x, y)
        print(f"CUDA operation successful. Result shape: {z.shape}")
        
        # Test complex tensor support
        complex_tensor = torch.complex(torch.rand(10, 10).cuda(), torch.rand(10, 10).cuda())
        print(f"Complex tensor on CUDA created. Shape: {complex_tensor.shape}")
        
        return True
    else:
        print("CUDA is not available")
        return False

verify_cuda()
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: CUDA shows available but operations fail
  - Restart kernel/Python interpreter
  - Check for CUDA out-of-memory errors
  - Verify CUDA driver and toolkit compatibility

- **Issue**: Complex tensors not supported
  - Ensure PyTorch version >= 1.9 for complex tensor support
  - Fallback to real tensors and manual complex arithmetic if needed

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder

def test_sequence_generation():
    config = LHLLMConfig()
    encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    
    # Generate sequence
    sequence = encoder.generate_sequence("Test prompt", n_tokens=100)
    
    # Check sequence properties
    valid = encoder.validate_sequence(sequence)
    info_density = encoder.get_information_density(sequence)
    
    # Print results
    print(f"Generated sequence of length {len(sequence)}")
    print(f"First 30 nucleotides: {sequence[:30]}")
    print(f"Sequence valid: {valid}")
    print(f"Information density: {info_density:.3f} bits/nt")
    
    # Test GC content
    gc_count = sum(1 for c in sequence if c in 'GC')
    gc_ratio = gc_count / len(sequence)
    
    print(f"GC content: {gc_ratio:.3f}")
    print(f"GC range: {config.gc_min:.3f} - {config.gc_max:.3f}")
    
    # Check homopolymer runs
    max_run = 1
    current_run = 1
    prev_nt = sequence[0]
    
    for nt in sequence[1:]:
        if nt == prev_nt:
            current_run += 1
            max_run = max(max_run, current_run)
        else:
            current_run = 1
        prev_nt = nt
    
    print(f"Maximum homopolymer run: {max_run}")
    print(f"Maximum allowed: {config.max_homopolymer}")
    
    # Verify fix_sequence works
    bad_sequence = "A" * 20 + "C" * 20 + "G" * 20 + "T" * 20
    print(f"\nBad sequence: {bad_sequence}")
    
    fixed = encoder.fix_sequence(bad_sequence)
    print(f"Fixed sequence: {fixed[:30]}...")
    print(f"Fixed sequence valid: {encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)}")
    
    return {
        "sequence_length": len(sequence),
        "is_valid": valid,
        "info_density": info_density,
        "gc_ratio": gc_ratio,
        "max_homopolymer_run": max_run,
        "fixed_sequence_valid": encoder.validate_sequence(fixed)
    }

test_results = test_sequence_generation()
print(f"Test results: {test_results}")

### 2.4 Harmonic Module Testing

Test the harmonic processing units with:

```python
import torch
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import LiquidODE, HarmonicFunction, HarmonicProcessingUnit, HPULayer

def test_liquid_neural_dynamics():
    # Test LiquidODE
    state_size = 16
    batch_size = 8
    liquid = LiquidODE(state_size=state_size, hidden_size=state_size*2)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, state_size)
    
    # Test forward pass
    h, y = liquid(x)
    
    print(f"LiquidODE test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Hidden state shape: {h.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    print(f"  Output range: [{y.min().item():.3f}, {y.max().item():.3f}]")
    
    # Test multiple time steps
    h_states = []
    h_current = None
    
    for t in range(10):
        h_current, y_current = liquid(x, h_current, dt=0.05)
        h_states.append(h_current.detach().cpu())
    
    h_trajectory = torch.stack(h_states, dim=0)  # [time, batch, hidden]
    
    print(f"  Multi-step trajectory shape: {h_trajectory.shape}")
    
    # Check if dynamics are changing (not stuck or exploding)
    h_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(h_trajectory[1:] - h_trajectory[:-1]))
    print(f"  Average state change per step: {h_diff.item():.5f}")
    
    if h_diff.item() < 1e-6:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics appear to be stuck (minimal state change)")
    elif h_diff.item() > 10.0:
        print("  WARNING: Dynamics may be unstable (large state changes)")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "hidden_shape": h.shape,
        "avg_state_change": h_diff.item()
    }

def test_harmonic_processing_unit():
    # Test HPU
    dim = 16
    batch_size = 8
    hpu = HarmonicProcessingUnit(dim=dim)
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, dim)
    
    # Test forward pass
    y = hpu(x)
    
    print(f"\nHPU test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {x.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {y.shape}")
    
    # Test quantum collapse behavior
    outputs = []
    
    for t in range(50):  # Should see collapse around 40Hz (~25ms)
        out = hpu(x, t=t*0.001, dt=0.001)
        outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
    
    outputs = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)  # [time, batch, dim]
    
    # Calculate temporal variations to detect collapse events
    output_diff = torch.abs(outputs[1:] - outputs[:-1])
    max_changes = torch.max(output_diff, dim=2)[0].mean(dim=1)
    
    # Collapse events should show as spikes in the derivative
    collapse_threshold = 0.1
    potential_collapses = torch.where(max_changes > collapse_threshold)[0]
    
    print(f"  Potential collapse events at time steps: {potential_collapses.tolist()}")
    print(f"  Expected collapse frequency: {hpu.or_frequency:.1f} Hz")
    print(f"  Expected collapses in this window: {50 * 0.001 * hpu.or_frequency:.1f}")
    
    # Check bioelectric component
    voltage_magnitude = torch.norm(hpu.voltage).item()
    print(f"  Voltage magnitude: {voltage_magnitude:.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": y.shape,
        "num_potential_collapses": len(potential_collapses),
        "voltage_magnitude": voltage_magnitude
    }

liquid_results = test_liquid_neural_dynamics()
hpu_results = test_harmonic_processing_unit()

print(f"\nLiquid neural dynamics test results: {liquid_results}")
print(f"HPU test results: {hpu_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Unstable dynamics in LiquidODE
  - Reduce initial weight scales (try 0.01, 0.001)
  - Add gradient clipping during training
  - Implement normalization of states

- **Issue**: Complex arithmetic errors
  - Check for NaN/Inf values in complex tensors
  - Verify complex tensor operations (avoid in-place operations)
  - Add small epsilon values to denominators

- **Issue**: Quantum collapse not occurring
  - Verify collapse threshold calculation
  - Check time tracking and accumulation
  - Trace probability calculations

from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import DigitalCell

def test_digital_cell():
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=32, num_cells=1)
    
    # Create digital cell
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0)
    
    # Test input
    batch_size = 4
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs, metrics = cell(inputs)
    
    print(f"Digital cell test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {outputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Metrics: {metrics}")
    
    # Test multiple time steps
    all_outputs = []
    all_metrics = []
    
    for t in range(10):
        out, met = cell(inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        all_outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
        all_metrics.append(met)
    
    # Check growth state progression
    growth_progression = [m['growth'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Growth state progression: {growth_progression}")
    
    # Check energy state
    energy_progression = [m['energy'] for m in all_metrics]
    print(f"  Energy progression: {energy_progression}")
    
    # Test cell division if growth is sufficient
    can_divide = cell.should_divide()
    print(f"  Cell ready to divide: {can_divide}")
    
    if can_divide:
        daughter = cell.divide()
        print(f"  Daughter cell created with ID: {daughter.cell_id}")
        
        # Verify daughter properties
        print(f"  Parent energy: {cell.energy.item():.3f}")
        print(f"  Daughter energy: {daughter.energy.item():.3f}")
        print(f"  Parent growth reset: {cell.growth_state.item():.3f}")
    
    return {
        "output_shape": outputs.shape,
        "metrics": metrics,
        "growth_progression": growth_progression,
        "energy_progression": energy_progression,
        "can_divide": can_divide
    }

cell_results = test_digital_cell()
print(f"\nDigital cell test results: {cell_results}")

def test_evaluation():
    """Test the evaluation function."""
    # Create a simple model for testing
    from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
    
    class SimpleModel(nn.Module):
        def __init__(self, config):
            super().__init__()
            self.config = config
            self.layers = nn.Sequential(
                nn.Linear(config.d_model, config.d_model * 2),
                nn.ReLU(),
                nn.Linear(config.d_model * 2, config.d_model)
            )
            
            # Add an organism attribute with required methods
            class MockOrganism:
                def get_state_matrix(self):
                    return torch.randn(32, 16)
                
                def get_adjacency_matrix(self):
                    adj = torch.randn(32, 32)
                    adj = (adj + adj.T) / 2  # Make symmetric
                    return torch.softmax(adj, dim=1)
            
            self.organism = MockOrganism()
        
        def forward(self, x, t=0.0, dt=0.01):
            output = self.layers(x[:, 0])  # Use only first token
            
            # Mock metrics
            coherence = torch.mean(torch.abs(torch.corrcoef(output)))
            phi = torch.mean(output) * 20.0
            avalanche_exponent = torch.tensor(1.5 + 0.1 * torch.sin(torch.tensor(t * 5.0)))
            energy_efficiency = torch.sigmoid(torch.mean(output))
            
            metrics = {
                "coherence": coherence.item(),
                "phi": phi.item(),
                "avalanche_exponent": avalanche_exponent.item(),
                "energy_efficiency": energy_efficiency.item()
            }
            
            return output, metrics
    
    # Create config
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=64)
    
    # Create model
    model = SimpleModel(config)
    
    # Create test inputs
    test_inputs = torch.randn(5, 10, config.d_model)
    
    # Run evaluation
    summary = evaluate_model(
        model,
        config,
        test_inputs=test_inputs,
        num_time_steps=10,
        output_dir="./test_evaluation"
    )
    
    print(f"\nEvaluation test:")
    print(f"  Mean coherence: {summary.get('coherence_mean', 0.0):.6f}")
    print(f"  Mean phi: {summary.get('phi_mean', 0.0):.6f}")
    print(f"  Mean evaluation time: {summary.get('mean_evaluation_time', 0.0):.6f}s")
    
    return summary

evaluation_results = test_evaluation()
print(f"\nEvaluation test results: {evaluation_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Missing metrics in output
  - Verify metric calculation functions are being called
  - Debug metric extraction from model
  - Add fallback values for missing metrics

- **Issue**: Slow evaluation
  - Profile time spent in each metric calculation
  - Implement caching for expensive metrics
  - Consider parallel evaluation

## 6. Common Issues and Solutions

### 6.1 GPU Memory Management

```python
def diagnose_gpu_memory_issues(model, example_input):
    """Diagnose GPU memory usage issues."""
    import torch
    import gc
    
    print("GPU Memory Diagnostics:")
    
    # Check if CUDA is available
    if not torch.cuda.is_available():
        print("  CUDA is not available")
        return
    
    # Get initial memory stats
    torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    gc.collect()
    
    initial_allocated = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    initial_reserved = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  Initial GPU memory allocated: {initial_allocated:.2f} MB")
    print(f"  Initial GPU memory reserved: {initial_reserved:.2f} MB")
    
    # Test model initialization memory usage
    model = model.to('cuda')
    
    after_model_allocated = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    after_model_reserved = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  After model to GPU:")
    print(f"    GPU memory allocated: {after_model_allocated:.2f} MB (+{after_model_allocated - initial_allocated:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"    GPU memory reserved: {after_model_reserved:.2f} MB (+{after_model_reserved - initial_reserved:.2f} MB)")
    
    # Test forward pass memory usage
    example_input = example_input.to('cuda')
    
    after_input_allocated = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    after_input_reserved = torch.cuda.memory_reserved() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  After input to GPU:")
    print(f"    GPU memory allocated: {after_input_allocated:.2f} MB (+{after_input_allocated - after_model_allocated:.2f} MB)")
    print(f"    GPU memory reserved: {after_input_reserved:.2f} MB (+{after_input_reserved - after_model_reserved:.2f} MB)")
    
    # Test forward pass
    torch.cuda.reset_peak_memory_stats()
    
    with torch.no_grad():
        output, _ = model(example_input)
    
    peak_allocated = torch.cuda.max_memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    current_allocated = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  After forward pass:")
    print(f"    Peak GPU memory allocated: {peak_allocated:.2f} MB")
    print(f"    Current GPU memory allocated: {current_allocated:.2f} MB")
    print(f"    Memory used during forward pass: {peak_allocated - after_input_allocated:.2f} MB")
    
    # Test backward pass
    torch.cuda.reset_peak_memory_stats()
    
    # Create a simple loss and backward
    loss = output.mean()
    loss.backward()
    
    peak_allocated_backward = torch.cuda.max_memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    current_allocated_backward = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  After backward pass:")
    print(f"    Peak GPU memory allocated: {peak_allocated_backward:.2f} MB")
    print(f"    Current GPU memory allocated: {current_allocated_backward:.2f} MB")
    print(f"    Memory used during backward pass: {peak_allocated_backward - current_allocated:.2f} MB")
    
    # Count parameters
    total_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters())
    trainable_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
    
    print(f"  Model parameters:")
    print(f"    Total parameters: {total_params:,}")
    print(f"    Trainable parameters: {trainable_params:,}")
    print(f"    Parameter memory: {total_params * 4 / 1024**2:.2f} MB (FP32)")
    
    # Check for memory leaks
    torch.cuda.empty_cache()
    gc.collect()
    
    final_allocated = torch.cuda.memory_allocated() / 1024**2
    
    print(f"  After cleanup:")
    print(f"    GPU memory allocated: {final_allocated:.2f} MB")
    
    if final_allocated > initial_allocated + 10:  # 10 MB threshold
        print(f"    Potential memory leak: {final_allocated - initial_allocated:.2f} MB not released")
        
        # Try to identify leak source
        print(f"    Performing object reference search...")
        for obj in gc.get_objects():
            try:
                if torch.is_tensor(obj) and obj.device.type == 'cuda':
                    print(f"      Found CUDA tensor: {obj.shape}, {obj.dtype}, requires_grad={obj.requires_grad}")
            except:
                pass
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: CUDA OOM errors
  - Apply `torch.cuda.empty_cache()` frequently
  - Use gradient checkpointing: `torch.utils.checkpoint.checkpoint()`
  - Implement model parallelism for large models

- **Issue**: Memory leaks
  - Watch for retained tensors with `requires_grad=True`
  - Check for tensors held in global variables or closures
  - Monitor tensors in custom cache implementations

### 6.2 Numerical Stability

```python
def diagnose_numerical_stability_issues(model, example_input, num_iterations=10):
    """Diagnose numerical stability issues."""
    import torch
    import numpy as np
    
    print("Numerical Stability Diagnostics:")
    
    # Move model and input to device
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    example_input = example_input.to(device)
    
    # Initialize stats tracking
    nans_detected = False
    infs_detected = False
    grad_stats = []
    
    # Run multiple iterations
    for i in range(num_iterations):
        # Zero gradients
        model.zero_grad()
        
        # Forward pass
        output, metrics = model(example_input)
        
        # Check for NaN/Inf in outputs
        if torch.isnan(output).any():
            print(f"  [Iteration {i}] NaN detected in model output")
            nans_detected = True
        
        if torch.isinf(output).any():
            print(f"  [Iteration {i}] Inf detected in model output")
            infs_detected = True
        
        # Check metrics
        for key, value in metrics.items():
            if isinstance(value, torch.Tensor):
                if torch.isnan(value).any():
                    print(f"  [Iteration {i}] NaN detected in metric '{key}'")
                    nans_detected = True
                
                if torch.isinf(value).any():
                    print(f"  [Iteration {i}] Inf detected in metric '{key}'")
                    infs_detected = True
        
        # Compute loss and backward
        loss = output.mean()
        loss.backward()
        
        # Check gradients
        grad_norms = []
        grad_max = []
        grad_has_nan = False
        grad_has_inf = False
        
        for name, param in model.parameters():
            if param.grad is not None:
                grad_norm = torch.norm(param.grad).item()
                grad_max_val = torch.max(torch.abs(param.grad)).item()
                
                grad_norms.append(grad_norm)
                grad_max.append(grad_max_val)
                
                if torch.isnan(param.grad).any():
                    print(f"  [Iteration {i}] NaN detected in gradients of '{name}'")
                    grad_has_nan = True
                
                if torch.isinf(param.grad).any():
                    print(f"  [Iteration {i}] Inf detected in gradients of '{name}'")
                    grad_has_inf = True
        
        # Record stats
        grad_stats.append({
            'mean_norm': np.mean(grad_norms),
            'max_norm': np.max(grad_norms),
            'max_value': np.max(grad_max),
            'has_nan': grad_has_nan,
            'has_inf': grad_has_inf
        })
    
    # Analyze gradient statistics
    mean_norms = [s['mean_norm'] for s in grad_stats]
    max_norms = [s['max_norm'] for s in grad_stats]
    max_values = [s['max_value'] for s in grad_stats]
    
    print("\n  Gradient Statistics:")
    print(f"    Mean gradient norm: {np.mean(mean_norms):.6f} ± {np.std(mean_norms):.6f}")
    print(f"    Max gradient norm: {np.max(max_norms):.6f}")
    print(f"    Max gradient value: {np.max(max_values):.6f}")
    
    # Check for exploding/vanishing gradients
    if np.max(max_values) > 100:
        print(f"    WARNING: Potentially exploding gradients detected (max value: {np.max(max_values):.2f})")
        print(f"    Consider using gradient clipping with torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_()")
    
    if np.mean(mean_norms) < 1e-7:
        print(f"    WARNING: Potentially vanishing gradients detected (mean norm: {np.mean(mean_norms):.2e})")
        print(f"    Consider adjusting initialization, optimizer, or model architecture")
    
    # Summary
    print("\n  Stability Summary:")
    print(f"    NaN values detected: {nans_detected}")
    print(f"    Inf values detected: {infs_detected}")
    
    if nans_detected or infs_detected:
        print("\n  Recommendations for NaN/Inf issues:")
        print("    - Check division by zero or log(0)")
        print("    - Add epsilon terms to denominators")
        print("    - Apply gradient clipping")
        print("    - Check initialization scales")
        print("    - Reduce learning rate")
        print("    - Consider using mixed precision training with dynamic scaling")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: NaN/Inf values
  - Add small epsilon values to divisions: `x / (y + 1e-8)`
  - Apply clipping to intermediate values
  - Debug complex number operations carefully

- **Issue**: Exploding gradients
  - Implement gradient clipping
  - Reduce learning rate
  - Check weight initialization scales

### 6.3 Complex-Valued Operations

```python
def diagnose_complex_tensor_issues(model):
    """Diagnose issues with complex-valued tensors."""
    import torch
    
    print("Complex Tensor Diagnostics:")
    
    # Check PyTorch version
    version = torch.__version__
    print(f"  PyTorch version: {version}")
    
    # Verify complex tensor support
    try:
        x = torch.complex(torch.randn(5), torch.randn(5))
        print(f"  Complex tensor support: Available")
    except:
        print(f"  Complex tensor support: NOT Available")
        print(f"  Upgrade to PyTorch 1.9+ for native complex tensor support")
        return
    
    # Test complex operations
    print("\n  Testing complex operations:")
    
    # Test complex matrix multiplication
    try:
        a = torch.complex(torch.randn(3, 4), torch.randn(3, 4))
        b = torch.complex(torch.randn(4, 5), torch.randn(4, 5))
        c = torch.matmul(a, b)
        print(f"    Complex matrix multiplication: OK")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"    Complex matrix multiplication failed: {e}")
    
    # Test complex in neural network
    try:
        class ComplexLinear(torch.nn.Module):
            def __init__(self):
                super().__init__()
                self.linear = torch.nn.Linear(4, 4, dtype=torch.complex64)
            
            def forward(self, x):
                return self.linear(x)
        
        complex_net = ComplexLinear()
        complex_input = torch.complex(torch.randn(2, 4), torch.randn(2, 4))
        complex_output = complex_net(complex_input)
        print(f"    Complex linear layer: OK")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"    Complex linear layer failed: {e}")
    
    # Test complex gradients
    try:
        x = torch.complex(torch.randn(5, requires_grad=True), torch.randn(5, requires_grad=True))
        y = x * x.conj()
        loss = y.real.sum()
        loss.backward()
        print(f"    Complex gradients: OK")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"    Complex gradients failed: {e}")
    
    # Check model for complex parameters
    complex_param_count = 0
    real_param_count = 0
    
    for name, param in model.named_parameters():
        if torch.is_complex(param):
            complex_param_count += 1
        else:
            real_param_count += 1
    
    print(f"\n  Model parameters:")
    print(f"    Complex-valued parameters: {complex_param_count}")
    print(f"    Real-valued parameters: {real_param_count}")
    
    if complex_param_count == 0:
        print(f"    WARNING: No complex parameters found in model")
    
    # Check if model has complex-specific handling
    has_complex_handling = False
    
    for attr_name in dir(model):
        attr = getattr(model, attr_name)
        if callable(attr) and 'complex' in attr_name.lower():
            has_complex_handling = True
            break
    
    print(f"    Complex-specific handling: {'Detected' if has_complex_handling else 'Not detected'}")
    
    # Recommendations
    print("\n  Recommendations for complex tensor usage:")
    print("    - Ensure all operations support complex tensors")
    print("    - Handle real/imaginary parts separately when needed")
    print("    - Be careful with in-place operations that may not support complex tensors")
    print("    - For activation functions, apply separately to real/imaginary parts if not holomorphic")
    print("    - When using norms, remember to use absolute value")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Complex tensor operation errors
  - Verify operation support for complex tensors
  - Implement custom complex-compatible activation functions
  - Apply operations to real and imaginary parts separately
  - Use absolute values for norms and magnitudes

- **Issue**: Complex gradient errors
  - Ensure loss function produces real values
  - Verify complex gradient flow through the model
  - Debug component by component

### 6.4 Integration Testing Utilities

Create comprehensive testing utilities:

```python
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Callable, Any

class TestHarness:
    """Test harness for comprehensive integration testing."""
    
    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, device: str = "cuda"):
        """
        Initialize the test harness.
        
        Args:
            model: Model to test
            device: Device to run tests on
        """
        self.model = model
        self.device = device
        self.tests = {}
        self.results = {}
    
    def add_test(self, name: str, test_fn: Callable, is_critical: bool = False):
        """
        Add a test to the harness.
        
        Args:
            name: Test name
            test_fn: Test function
            is_critical: Whether test is critical (failure stops testing)
        """
        self.tests[name] = {
            "function": test_fn,
            "is_critical": is_critical
        }
    
    def run_tests(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """
        Run all tests.
        
        Returns:
            Dictionary of test results
        """
        self.results = {}
        
        for name, test_info in self.tests.items():
            print(f"Running test: {name}")
            try:
                result = test_info["function"](self.model)
                self.results[name] = {
                    "success": True,
                    "result": result
                }
                print(f"  Test passed")
            except Exception as e:
                self.results[name] = {
                    "success": False,
                    "error": str(e)
                }
                print(f"  Test failed: {e}")
                
                if test_info["is_critical"]:
                    print(f"  Critical test failed. Stopping testing.")
                    break
        
        # Calculate summary
        total_tests = len(self.results)
        passed_tests = sum(1 for r in self.results.values() if r["success"])
        
        print(f"\nTest Summary:")
        print(f"  Total tests: {total_tests}")
        print(f"  Passed: {passed_tests}")
        print(f"  Failed: {total_tests - passed_tests}")
        
        if passed_tests == total_tests:
            print(f"  All tests passed!")
        
        return self.results
    
    def generate_report(self, output_file: str = "test_report.txt"):
        """
        Generate a test report.
        
        Args:
            output_file: Output file name
        """
        with open(output_file, "w") as f:
            f.write("# LH-LLM Test Report\n\n")
            
            # Write summary
            total_tests = len(self.results)
            passed_tests = sum(1 for r in self.results.values() if r["success"])
            
            f.write(f"## Summary\n\n")
            f.write(f"- Total tests: {total_tests}\n")
            f.write(f"- Passed: {passed_tests}\n")
            f.write(f"- Failed: {total_tests - passed_tests}\n\n")
            
            # Write detailed results
            f.write(f"## Detailed Results\n\n")
            
            for name, result in self.results.items():
                f.write(f"### {name}\n\n")
                
                if result["success"]:
                    f.write(f"- Status: ✅ PASSED\n")
                    f.write(f"- Result: {result['result']}\n\n")
                else:
                    f.write(f"- Status: ❌ FAILED\n")
                    f.write(f"- Error: {result['error']}\n\n")
        
        print(f"Test report generated: {output_file}")


# Common test functions
def test_forward_pass(model: nn.Module) -> Dict:
    """Test basic forward pass."""
    # Get device and dimensions from model
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    
    # Try to determine input shape from model
    if hasattr(model, 'config') and hasattr(model.config, 'd_model'):
        d_model = model.config.d_model
    else:
        d_model = 64  # default
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(2, 10, d_model, device=device)
    
    # Forward pass
    with torch.no_grad():
        outputs, metrics = model(x)
    
    # Check outputs
    assert outputs is not None, "Model output is None"
    assert isinstance(metrics, dict), "Metrics should be a dictionary"
    
    return {
        "output_shape": list(outputs.shape),
        "metrics_keys": list(metrics.keys())
    }

def test_gradient_flow(model: nn.Module) -> Dict:
    """Test gradient flow."""
    # Get device and dimensions from model
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    
    # Try to determine input shape from model
    if hasattr(model, 'config') and hasattr(model.config, 'd_model'):
        d_model = model.config.d_model
    else:
        d_model = 64  # default
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(2, 10, d_model, device=device)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs, _ = model(x)
    
    # Compute loss
    loss = outputs.mean()
    
    # Backward pass
    loss.backward()
    
    # Check gradients
    grad_norms = {}
    all_zero = True
    
    for name, param in model.named_parameters():
        if param.requires_grad:
            if param.grad is not None:
                grad_norm = torch.norm(param.grad).item()
                grad_norms[name] = grad_norm
                
                if grad_norm > 0:
                    all_zero = False
    
    assert not all_zero, "All gradients are zero"
    
    return {
        "grad_norms": grad_norms,
        "max_grad": max(grad_norms.values()) if grad_norms else 0
    }

def test_stateful_behavior(model: nn.Module) -> Dict:
    """Test stateful behavior over time steps."""
    # Get device and dimensions from model
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    
    # Try to determine input shape from model
    if hasattr(model, 'config') and hasattr(model.config, 'd_model'):
        d_model = model.config.d_model
    else:
        d_model = 64  # default
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(2, 10, d_model, device=device)
    
    # Run model for multiple time steps
    outputs = []
    metrics_list = []
    
    with torch.no_grad():
        for t in range(5):
            out, metrics = model(x, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
            outputs.append(out.detach().cpu())
            metrics_list.append(metrics)
    
    # Check for changes over time
    outputs_tensor = torch.stack(outputs, dim=0)
    output_diff = torch.mean(torch.abs(outputs_tensor[1:] - outputs_tensor[:-1])).item()
    
    # Check for changes in metrics
    metric_changes = {}
    for key in metrics_list[0].keys():
        if all(key in m for m in metrics_list):
            values = [m[key] for m in metrics_list if isinstance(m[key], (int, float, bool)) or
                     (isinstance(m[key], torch.Tensor) and m[key].numel() == 1)]
            
            if len(values) > 1:
                if all(isinstance(v, torch.Tensor) for v in values):
                    values = [v.item() for v in values]
                
                if len(values) > 1:
                    metric_changes[key] = max(values) - min(values)
    
    assert output_diff > 0, "Outputs do not change over time steps"
    
    return {
        "output_diff": output_diff,
        "metric_changes": metric_changes
    }

def test_quantum_like_properties(model: nn.Module) -> Dict:
    """Test quantum-like properties."""
    # This is a specialized test for the LH-LLM which has quantum-inspired components
    
    # Get device and dimensions from model
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    
    # Try to determine input shape from model
    if hasattr(model, 'config') and hasattr(model.config, 'd_model'):
        d_model = model.config.d_model
    else:
        d_model = 64  # default
    
    # Create test input
    x = torch.randn(2, 10, d_model, device=device)
    
    # Test collapse behavior
    collapse_detected = False
    quantum_metrics = []
    
    with torch.no_grad():
        # Run for more steps to ensure collapse happens
        for t in range(50):
            _, metrics = model(x, t=t*0.001, dt=0.001)
            
            # Store quantum-related metrics
            if "quantum_fidelity" in metrics:
                quantum_metrics.append(metrics["quantum_fidelity"])
            
            # Look for collapse-related metrics
            if "collapse_event" in metrics and metrics["collapse_event"]:
                collapse_detected = True
                break
    
    # Check if model has quantum components
    has_quantum_components = False
    
    for name, module in model.named_modules():
        if "quantum" in name.lower() or "hpu" in name.lower():
            has_quantum_components = True
            break
    
    return {
        "has_quantum_components": has_quantum_components,
        "collapse_detected": collapse_detected,
        "quantum_metrics": quantum_metrics
    }

def run_integration_tests(model: nn.Module) -> Dict:
    """Run a full suite of integration tests."""
    test_harness = TestHarness(model)
    
    # Add tests
    test_harness.add_test("forward_pass", test_forward_pass, is_critical=True)
    test_harness.add_test("gradient_flow", test_gradient_flow)
    test_harness.add_test("stateful_behavior", test_stateful_behavior)
    test_harness.add_test("quantum_properties", test_quantum_like_properties)
    
    # Add diagnoses
    test_harness.add_test("numerical_stability", lambda m: diagnose_numerical_stability_issues(m, torch.randn(2, 10, 64)))
    
    if torch.cuda.is_available():
        test_harness.add_test("gpu_memory", lambda m: diagnose_gpu_memory_issues(m, torch.randn(2, 10, 64)))
    
    test_harness.add_test("complex_tensors", diagnose_complex_tensor_issues)
    
    # Run tests
    results = test_harness.run_tests()
    
    # Generate report
    test_harness.generate_report("integration_test_report.txt")
    
    return results
```

This comprehensive development and debugging guide provides step-by-step instructions for implementing and troubleshooting the Liquid Harmonic Large Language Model (LH-LLM). By following these guidelines and using the diagnostic tools provided, you can efficiently develop, debug, and optimize this advanced bio-inspired neural architecture.

The guide is structured to help both human developers and LLM assistants understand the system's components, identify common issues, and implement effective solutions throughout the development process.
    def _apply_diffusion_evolution(self):
        """Apply diffusion evolution to model parameters."""
        if self.diffusion_evolution is None:
            return False
        
        # Extract model parameters
        param_vector = []
        param_shapes = []
        
        for name, param in self.model.named_parameters():
            if param.requires_grad:
                param_shapes.append((name, param.shape, param.numel()))
                param_vector.append(param.data.view(-1))
        
        # Concatenate parameters into a single vector
        all_params = torch.cat(param_vector)
        
        # Create fitness function
        def fitness_fn(params_batch):
            fitness_values = []
            
            # Process each parameter set in the batch
            for params in params_batch:
                # Copy parameters to model
                offset = 0
                for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
                    param_data = params[offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
                    offset += numel
                    
                    # Find parameter in model
                    for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                        if n == name:
                            p.data.copy_(param_data)
                            break
                
                # Forward pass
                with torch.no_grad():
                    batch = self._get_batch(2, self._get_current_curriculum()["complexity"])
                    outputs, metrics = self.model(batch["input"])
                    
                # Calculate fitness
                fitness = self._calculate_fitness(metrics)
                fitness_values.append(fitness)
            
            return torch.tensor(fitness_values, device=params_batch.device)
        
        # Apply diffusion evolution
        evolved_params = self.diffusion_evolution.evolve(
            all_params.unsqueeze(0), 
            fitness_fn
        )
        
        # Update model with evolved parameters
        offset = 0
        for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
            param_data = evolved_params[0, offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
            offset += numel
            
            # Find parameter in model
            for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                if n == name:
                    p.data.copy_(param_data)
                    break
        
        return True
    
    def _apply_nsga_optimization(self):
        """Apply NSGA-II optimization to model parameters."""
        if self.nsga_optimizer is None:
            return False
        
        # Extract model parameters
        param_vector = []
        param_shapes = []
        
        for name, param in self.model.named_parameters():
            if param.requires_grad:
                param_shapes.append((name, param.shape, param.numel()))
                param_vector.append(param.data.view(-1))
        
        # Concatenate parameters into a single vector
        all_params = torch.cat(param_vector)
        
        # Create initial population
        population_size = self.nsga_optimizer.population_size
        population = all_params.unsqueeze(0).expand(population_size, -1).clone()
        
        # Add noise to create diverse population
        noise = torch.randn_like(population) * 0.01
        population = population + noise
        
        # Define objective functions
        objective_functions = []
        
        # Objective 1: Coherence
        def coherence_objective(params_batch):
            values = []
            
            for params in params_batch:
                # Copy parameters to model
                offset = 0
                for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
                    param_data = params[offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
                    offset += numel
                    
                    # Find parameter in model
                    for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                        if n == name:
                            p.data.copy_(param_data)
                            break
                
                # Forward pass
                with torch.no_grad():
                    batch = self._get_batch(2, self._get_current_curriculum()["complexity"])
                    outputs, metrics = self.model(batch["input"])
                
                # Get coherence value
                coherence = metrics.get("coherence", torch.tensor(0.0))
                if isinstance(coherence, torch.Tensor):
                    coherence = coherence.item()
                
                values.append(coherence)
            
            return torch.tensor(values, device=params_batch.device)
        
        # Objective 2: Phi (integrated information)
        def phi_objective(params_batch):
            values = []
            
            for params in params_batch:
                # Copy parameters to model
                offset = 0
                for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
                    param_data = params[offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
                    offset += numel
                    
                    # Find parameter in model
                    for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                        if n == name:
                            p.data.copy_(param_data)
                            break
                
                # Forward pass
                with torch.no_grad():
                    batch = self._get_batch(2, self._get_current_curriculum()["complexity"])
                    outputs, metrics = self.model(batch["input"])
                
                # Get phi value
                phi = metrics.get("phi", torch.tensor(0.0))
                if isinstance(phi, torch.Tensor):
                    phi = phi.item()
                
                values.append(phi)
            
            return torch.tensor(values, device=params_batch.device)
        
        # Objective 3: Energy efficiency
        def energy_objective(params_batch):
            values = []
            
            for params in params_batch:
                # Copy parameters to model
                offset = 0
                for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
                    param_data = params[offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
                    offset += numel
                    
                    # Find parameter in model
                    for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                        if n == name:
                            p.data.copy_(param_data)
                            break
                
                # Forward pass
                with torch.no_grad():
                    batch = self._get_batch(2, self._get_current_curriculum()["complexity"])
                    outputs, metrics = self.model(batch["input"])
                
                # Get energy efficiency value
                energy = metrics.get("energy_efficiency", torch.tensor(0.0))
                if isinstance(energy, torch.Tensor):
                    energy = energy.item()
                
                values.append(energy)
            
            return torch.tensor(values, device=params_batch.device)
        
        objective_functions = [coherence_objective, phi_objective, energy_objective]
        
        # Run NSGA-II optimization
        pareto_set, pareto_front = self.nsga_optimizer.optimize(
            population,
            objective_functions,
            num_generations=5  # Small number for training iteration
        )
        
        # Select the solution with the best average ranking
        avg_rank = torch.mean(torch.argsort(torch.argsort(pareto_front, dim=0), dim=0).float(), dim=1)
        best_idx = torch.argmin(avg_rank).item()
        best_solution = pareto_set[best_idx]
        
        # Update model with best solution
        offset = 0
        for name, shape, numel in param_shapes:
            param_data = best_solution[offset:offset + numel].view(shape)
            offset += numel
            
            # Find parameter in model
            for n, p in self.model.named_parameters():
                if n == name:
                    p.data.copy_(param_data)
                    break
        
        return True
    
    def train(self, num_iterations=None):
        """
        Train the model.
        
        Args:
            num_iterations: Number of training iterations (default: config.max_iterations)
        """
        if num_iterations is None:
            num_iterations = self.config.max_iterations
        
        # Track best fitness
        best_fitness = -float('inf')
        
        # Start training loop
        print(f"Starting training for {num_iterations} iterations")
        print(f"Initial curriculum stage: {self._get_current_curriculum()['name']}")
        print(f"Complexity: {self._get_current_curriculum()['complexity']}")
        
        no_improvement_count = 0
        
        for iteration in tqdm(range(self.current_iteration, self.current_iteration + num_iterations)):
            self.current_iteration = iteration
            
            # Update curriculum if needed
            self._update_curriculum()
            
            # Get current curriculum complexity
            complexity = self._get_current_curriculum()["complexity"]
            
            # Start timer
            start_time = time.time()
            
            # Get batch
            batch = self._get_batch(self.config.batch_size, complexity)
            
            # Forward pass
            self.model.train()
            outputs, metrics = self.model(batch["input"])
            
            # Calculate loss
            loss = self._calculate_loss(outputs, metrics, batch)
            
            # Backward pass and optimize
            self.optimizer.zero_grad()
            loss.backward()
            torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(self.model.parameters(), self.config.gradient_clip)
            self.optimizer.step()
            
            # Apply evolution every 10 iterations
            if iteration % 10 == 0:
                # Apply diffusion evolution
                if hasattr(self, 'diffusion_evolution') and self.diffusion_evolution is not None:
                    self._apply_diffusion_evolution()
                
                # Apply NSGA-II optimization
                if hasattr(self, 'nsga_optimizer') and self.nsga_optimizer is not None:
                    self._apply_nsga_optimization()
            
            # Calculate fitness
            fitness = self._calculate_fitness(metrics)
            
            # End timer
            end_time = time.time()
            iteration_time = end_time - start_time
            
            # Update metrics history
            self.metrics_history["train_loss"].append(loss.item())
            self.metrics_history["fitness"].append(fitness)
            self.metrics_history["coherence"].append(metrics.get("coherence", 0.0))
            self.metrics_history["phi"].append(metrics.get("phi", 0.0))
            self.metrics_history["avalanche_exponent"].append(metrics.get("avalanche_exponent", 1.5))
            self.metrics_history["energy_efficiency"].append(metrics.get("energy_efficiency", 0.0))
            self.metrics_history["iteration_time"].append(iteration_time)
            
            # Check for best model
            is_best = fitness > best_fitness
            if is_best:
                best_fitness = fitness
                no_improvement_count = 0
                
                # Update best metrics
                self.best_metrics["fitness"] = fitness
                self.best_metrics["coherence"] = metrics.get("coherence", 0.0)
                self.best_metrics["phi"] = metrics.get("phi", 0.0)
                
                # Save best checkpoint
                self._save_checkpoint(metrics, is_best=True)
            else:
                no_improvement_count += 1
            
            # Save periodic checkpoint
            if iteration % 50 == 0:
                self._save_checkpoint(metrics)
                self._save_metrics()
            
            # Log metrics
            if iteration % 10 == 0:
                print(f"\nIteration {iteration}:")
                print(f"  Loss: {loss.item():.6f}")
                print(f"  Fitness: {fitness:.6f}")
                print(f"  Coherence: {metrics.get('coherence', 0.0):.6f}")
                print(f"  Phi: {metrics.get('phi', 0.0):.6f}")
                print(f"  Avalanche exponent: {metrics.get('avalanche_exponent', 1.5):.6f}")
                print(f"  Energy efficiency: {metrics.get('energy_efficiency', 0.0):.6f}")
                print(f"  Iteration time: {iteration_time:.2f}s")
            
            # Check early stopping
            if no_improvement_count >= self.config.early_stopping_patience:
                print(f"\nEarly stopping triggered after {no_improvement_count} iterations without improvement")
                break
        
        # Final save
        self._save_checkpoint(metrics)
        self._save_metrics()
        
        print(f"\nTraining completed:")
        print(f"  Best fitness: {best_fitness:.6f}")
        print(f"  Best coherence: {self.best_metrics['coherence']:.6f}")
        print(f"  Best phi: {self.best_metrics['phi']:.6f}")
        
        return self.metrics_history

def test_training():
    """Test the training loop."""
    # Create a simple model for testing
    from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
    
    class SimpleModel(nn.Module):
        def __init__(self, config):
            super().__init__()
            self.config = config
            self.layers = nn.Sequential(
                nn.Linear(config.d_model, config.d_model * 2),
                nn.ReLU(),
                nn.Linear(config.d_model * 2, config.d_model)
            )
        
        def forward(self, x):
            output = self.layers(x)
            
            # Mock metrics
            coherence = torch.mean(torch.abs(torch.corrcoef(output)))
            phi = torch.mean(output) * 20.0
            avalanche_exponent = torch.tensor(1.5)
            energy_efficiency = torch.sigmoid(torch.mean(output))
            
            metrics = {
                "coherence": coherence,
                "phi": phi,
                "avalanche_exponent": avalanche_exponent,
                "energy_efficiency": energy_efficiency
            }
            
            return output, metrics
    
    # Create config
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=64,
        max_iterations=100,
        early_stopping_patience=20,
        learning_rate=1e-4
    )
    
    # Create model
    model = SimpleModel(config)
    
    # Create trainer
    trainer = Trainer(model, config, save_dir="./simple_training")
    
    # Train for a few iterations
    history = trainer.train(num_iterations=20)
    
    print(f"\nTraining test:")
    print(f"  Final loss: {history['train_loss'][-1]:.6f}")
    print(f"  Final fitness: {history['fitness'][-1]:.6f}")
    print(f"  Training time: {sum(history['iteration_time']):.2f}s")
    
    return {
        "final_loss": history['train_loss'][-1],
        "final_fitness": history['fitness'][-1],
        "num_iterations": len(history['train_loss']),
        "training_time": sum(history['iteration_time'])
    }

training_results = test_training()
print(f"\nTraining test results: {training_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Slow training iterations
  - Profile memory and computation bottlenecks
  - Implement mixed precision training
  - Optimize batch size and model components

- **Issue**: Unstable fitness metrics
  - Normalize fitness components
  - Implement moving average for metrics
  - Debug individual metric calculations

- **Issue**: CUDA out-of-memory errors
  - Add memory profiling with `torch.cuda.memory_summary()`
  - Implement gradient checkpointing
  - Reduce model size during development

## 5. System Evaluation

### 5.1 Metrics Implementation

Implement advanced consciousness-like metrics:

```python
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple

class ConsciousnessMetrics:
    """Metrics for evaluating consciousness-like properties."""
    
    @staticmethod
    def integrated_information(connectivity_matrix: torch.Tensor, state: torch.Tensor) -> float:
        """
        Calculate integrated information (Phi) from connectivity and state.
        
        This is a simplified approximation of the full Phi calculation,
        which is computationally intensive for large systems.
        
        Args:
            connectivity_matrix: Connectivity between elements (N x N)
            state: Current state of elements (N x D)
            
        Returns:
            Integrated information (Phi) value
        """
        # Convert to numpy for graph operations
        if isinstance(connectivity_matrix, torch.Tensor):
            conn_np = connectivity_matrix.detach().cpu().numpy()
        else:
            conn_np = connectivity_matrix
        
        # Create graph
        G = nx.from_numpy_array(conn_np)
        
        # Calculate graph metrics
        clustering = nx.average_clustering(G)
        try:
            path_length = nx.average_shortest_path_length(G)
        except nx.NetworkXError:
            # Graph may not be connected
            path_length = np.mean([
                nx.average_shortest_path_length(G.subgraph(c))
                for c in nx.connected_components(G)
                if len(c) > 1
            ])
        
        # Calculate small-world index (approximation)
        # Higher values indicate more small-world topology
        # which correlates with integrated information
        rand_path = np.log(G.number_of_nodes())
        rand_cluster = G.number_of_edges() / (G.number_of_nodes() * (G.number_of_nodes() - 1))
        
        small_world_index = (clustering / rand_cluster) / (path_length / rand_path)
        
        # Calculate state differentiation
        if isinstance(state, torch.Tensor):
            state_np = state.detach().cpu().numpy()
        else:
            state_np = state
        
        # Calculate correlation or mutual information
        try:
            correlation = np.corrcoef(state_np)
            # Remove NaN values
            correlation = np.nan_to_num(correlation)
            
            # Calculate mean absolute correlation excluding diagonal
            n = correlation.shape[0]
            mean_corr = (np.sum(np.abs(correlation)) - n) / (n * n - n)
        except:
            mean_corr = 0.0
        
        # Combine metrics into Phi approximation
        # This is a heuristic approximation, not the formal Phi calculation
        phi = 10.0 * small_world_index * mean_corr * (1 - 1.0 / path_length)
        
        # Scale to typical Phi values observed in literature
        scaled_phi = phi * 20.0
        
        return float(scaled_phi)
    
    @staticmethod
    def information_closure(state: torch.Tensor, state_history: List[torch.Tensor]) -> float:
        """
        Calculate information closure from state history.
        
        Information closure measures the degree to which a system's
        state can be predicted from its own past states, rather than
        requiring information about external influences.
        
        Args:
            state: Current state tensor
            state_history: List of previous state tensors
            
        Returns:
            Information closure value
        """
        if len(state_history) < 2:
            return 0.0
        
        # Convert states to numpy
        if isinstance(state, torch.Tensor):
            current = state.detach().cpu().numpy()
        else:
            current = state
        
        # Concatenate history into a matrix
        history = []
        for s in state_history:
            if isinstance(s, torch.Tensor):
                history.append(s.detach().cpu().numpy())
            else:
                history.append(s)
        
        history_matrix = np.stack(history, axis=0)
        
        # Calculate autocorrelation with lag 1
        try:
            # Flatten each state
            flat_history = history_matrix.reshape(len(state_history), -1)
            flat_current = current.reshape(1, -1)
            
            # Calculate correlation
            corr_matrix = np.corrcoef(flat_history, flat_current)
            
            # Extract correlations with current state
            correlations = corr_matrix[-1, :-1]
            
            # Calculate weighted sum of correlations (more weight to recent states)
            weights = np.exp(-np.arange(len(correlations))[::-1] / 3.0)
            weights = weights / weights.sum()
            
            weighted_correlation = np.sum(np.abs(correlations) * weights)
            
            # Normalize to [0, 1] range
            normalized = weighted_correlation
        except:
            normalized = 0.0
        
        return float(normalized)
    
    @staticmethod
    def causal_density(connectivity_matrix: torch.Tensor, states: List[torch.Tensor]) -> float:
        """
        Calculate causal density from connectivity and state history.
        
        Causal density measures the overall strength of causal interactions
        between system elements, normalized by the number of elements.
        
        Args:
            connectivity_matrix: Connectivity between elements
            states: List of state tensors over time
            
        Returns:
            Causal density value
        """
        if len(states) < 3:
            return 0.0
        
        # Convert to numpy
        if isinstance(connectivity_matrix, torch.Tensor):
            conn_np = connectivity_matrix.detach().cpu().numpy()
        else:
            conn_np = connectivity_matrix
        
        # Create weighted graph
        G = nx.from_numpy_array(conn_np, create_using=nx.DiGraph)
        
        # Calculate graph theory metrics
        try:
            # PageRank centrality correlates with causal influence
            pageranks = nx.pagerank(G, alpha=0.85)
            
            # Calculate variance of centrality (higher variance = more causal structure)
            centrality_variance = np.var(list(pageranks.values()))
            
            # Scale to reasonable range
            scaled_variance = centrality_variance * 100.0
            
            # Apply nonlinearity for better scaling
            causal_density = 1.0 - np.exp(-scaled_variance)
        except:
            causal_density = 0.0
        
        return float(causal_density)
    
    @staticmethod
    def calculate_all_metrics(model, inputs, num_steps=10) -> Dict[str, float]:
        """
        Calculate all consciousness-like metrics for a model.
        
        Args:
            model: Model to evaluate
            inputs: Input tensor
            num_steps: Number of steps to run
            
        Returns:
            Dictionary of metrics
        """
        model.eval()
        
        # Run model for multiple steps to collect states
        states = []
        adjacency = None
        
        with torch.no_grad():
            for i in range(num_steps):
                outputs, metrics = model(inputs, t=i*0.01, dt=0.01)
                
                # Extract state representation
                if hasattr(model, 'organism') and hasattr(model.organism, 'get_state_matrix'):
                    state = model.organism.get_state_matrix()
                    states.append(state)
                
                # Extract adjacency matrix
                if adjacency is None and hasattr(model, 'organism') and hasattr(model.organism, 'get_adjacency_matrix'):
                    adjacency = model.organism.get_adjacency_matrix()
        
        # Calculate metrics
