        result_metrics = {}
        
        # If we have states and adjacency
        if states and adjacency is not None:
            # Integrated information
            phi = ConsciousnessMetrics.integrated_information(adjacency, states[-1])
            result_metrics["phi"] = phi
            
            # Information closure
            closure = ConsciousnessMetrics.information_closure(states[-1], states[:-1])
            result_metrics["information_closure"] = closure
            
            # Causal density
            density = ConsciousnessMetrics.causal_density(adjacency, states)
            result_metrics["causal_density"] = density
        
        # Add basic metrics from model if available
        if len(metrics) > 0:
            for key, value in metrics.items():
                if isinstance(value, (int, float, bool)):
                    result_metrics[key] = value
                elif isinstance(value, torch.Tensor) and value.numel() == 1:
                    result_metrics[key] = value.item()
        
        return result_metrics

def test_consciousness_metrics():
    """Test consciousness metrics calculation."""
    # Create random connectivity and state
    n = 32  # Number of elements
    d = 16  # State dimension
    
    connectivity = torch.randn(n, n)
    connectivity = (connectivity + connectivity.T) / 2  # Make symmetric
    connectivity = torch.softmax(connectivity, dim=1)  # Normalize
    
    states = [torch.randn(n, d) for _ in range(5)]
    
    # Calculate metrics
    phi = ConsciousnessMetrics.integrated_information(connectivity, states[-1])
    closure = ConsciousnessMetrics.information_closure(states[-1], states[:-1])
    density = ConsciousnessMetrics.causal_density(connectivity, states)
    
    print(f"Consciousness metrics test:")
    print(f"  Integrated information (Phi): {phi:.6f}")
    print(f"  Information closure: {closure:.6f}")
    print(f"  Causal density: {density:.6f}")
    
    # Test with different network structures
    # Create a more modular network
    modular_connectivity = torch.zeros(n, n)
    module_size = 8
    for i in range(n // module_size):
        start = i * module_size
        end = (i + 1) * module_size
        modular_connectivity[start:end, start:end] = torch.softmax(torch.randn(module_size, module_size), dim=1)
    
    # Add some inter-module connections
    modular_connectivity += torch.randn(n, n) * 0.05
    modular_connectivity = torch.softmax(modular_connectivity, dim=1)
    
    # Calculate metrics for modular network
    modular_phi = ConsciousnessMetrics.integrated_information(modular_connectivity, states[-1])
    
    print(f"\n  Modular network Phi: {modular_phi:.6f}")
    print(f"  Difference from random network: {modular_phi - phi:.6f}")
    
    return {
        "phi": phi,
        "information_closure": closure,
        "causal_density": density,
        "modular_phi": modular_phi
    }

metrics_test_results = test_consciousness_metrics()
print(f"\nConsciousness metrics test results: {metrics_test_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: NaN/Inf values in metrics
  - Add error handling for numerical instabilities
  - Check for division by zero
  - Add more detailed logging for metric calculation steps

- **Issue**: Unrealistic Phi values
  - Verify graph theory calculations
  - Debug normalization steps
  - Compare to published reference values

### 5.2 Model Evaluation

Implement model evaluation function:

```python
import torch
import time
import json
import pandas as pd
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def evaluate_model(
    model,
    config,
    test_inputs: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None,
    num_test_samples: int = 10,
    num_time_steps: int = 20,
    output_dir: str = "./evaluation"
):
    """
    Comprehensive evaluation of an LH-LLM model.
    
    Args:
        model: Model to evaluate
        config: Configuration object
        test_inputs: Optional specific test inputs
        num_test_samples: Number of test samples to generate if test_inputs not provided
        num_time_steps: Number of time steps to evaluate
        output_dir: Directory for output files
        
    Returns:
        Dictionary of evaluation results
    """
    output_path = Path(output_dir)
    output_path.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    
    model.eval()
    device = next(model.parameters()).device
    
    # Generate test inputs if not provided
    if test_inputs is None:
        test_inputs = torch.randn(num_test_samples, 10, config.d_model, device=device)
    
    # Metrics to track
    all_metrics = []
    all_evaluation_times = []
    
    # Consciousness metrics
    consciousness_metrics = ConsciousnessMetrics()
    
    # Run evaluation over time steps
    print(f"Evaluating model over {num_time_steps} time steps")
    
    for t in range(num_time_steps):
        start_time = time.time()
        
        # Forward pass
        with torch.no_grad():
            outputs, metrics = model(test_inputs, t=t*0.01, dt=0.01)
        
        # Calculate consciousness metrics
        if t % 5 == 0:  # Calculate every 5 steps to save time
            cm = consciousness_metrics.calculate_all_metrics(model, test_inputs, num_steps=5)
            metrics.update(cm)
        
        # Record evaluation time
        eval_time = time.time() - start_time
        all_evaluation_times.append(eval_time)
        
        # Add time step to metrics
        metrics["time_step"] = t
        all_metrics.append(metrics)
        
        if t % 5 == 0:
            print(f"  Time step {t}: evaluation time = {eval_time:.4f}s")
            for key, value in sorted(metrics.items()):
                if isinstance(value, (int, float)) and not key.startswith("_"):
                    print(f"    {key}: {value:.6f}")
    
    # Convert metrics to DataFrame
    metrics_df = pd.DataFrame(all_metrics)
    
    # Save metrics to CSV
    metrics_df.to_csv(output_path / "evaluation_metrics.csv", index=False)
    
    # Calculate summary statistics
    summary = {}
    
    for column in metrics_df.columns:
        if column != "time_step" and metrics_df[column].dtype in [float, int]:
            summary[f"{column}_mean"] = metrics_df[column].mean()
            summary[f"{column}_std"] = metrics_df[column].std()
            summary[f"{column}_min"] = metrics_df[column].min()
            summary[f"{column}_max"] = metrics_df[column].max()
    
    # Add evaluation metadata
    summary["num_time_steps"] = num_time_steps
    summary["num_test_samples"] = len(test_inputs)
    summary["mean_evaluation_time"] = np.mean(all_evaluation_times)
    
    # Save summary
    with open(output_path / "evaluation_summary.json", "w") as f:
        json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
    
    # Plot metrics over time
    plt.figure(figsize=(15, 10))
    
    # Key metrics to plot
    key_metrics = ["coherence", "phi", "avalanche_exponent", "energy_efficiency"]
    
    for i, metric in enumerate(key_metrics):
        if metric in metrics_df.columns:
            plt.subplot(2, 2, i+1)
            plt.plot(metrics_df["time_step"], metrics_df[metric])
            plt.title(f"{metric.capitalize()}")
            plt.xlabel("Time Step")
            plt.ylabel("Value")
    
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.savefig(output_path / "metrics_over_time.png")
    plt.close        # Create time embedding
        t_embed = torch.ones(noisy_z.shape[0], 1, device=self.device) * t / self.num_steps
        
        # Predict noise
        predicted_noise = self.denoiser(torch.cat([noisy_z, t_embed], dim=1))
        
        # Get alpha and beta for current step
        alpha = self.alphas[t]
        beta = self.betas[t]
        
        # Compute denoised latent (reverse diffusion step)
        denoised_z = (noisy_z - beta * predicted_noise / torch.sqrt(1 - self.alphas_cumprod[t])) / torch.sqrt(alpha)
        
        return denoised_z
    
    def sample(self, num_samples: int = 1) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Sample parameters using diffusion.
        
        Args:
            num_samples: Number of samples to generate
            
        Returns:
            Sampled parameter tensor
        """
        # Start from random noise
        z = torch.randn(num_samples, self.latent_dim, device=self.device)
        
        # Iteratively denoise
        for t in reversed(range(self.num_steps)):
            z = self.denoise_step(z, t)
        
        # Decode to parameter space
        params = self.decoder(z)
        
        return params
    
    def evolve(self, params: torch.Tensor, fitness_fn: Callable, num_steps: int = None) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Evolve parameters using diffusion and fitness selection.
        
        Args:
            params: Initial parameter tensor
            fitness_fn: Function to evaluate fitness of parameters
            num_steps: Number of diffusion steps (default: self.num_steps)
            
        Returns:
            Evolved parameter tensor
        """
        if num_steps is None:
            num_steps = self.num_steps
        
        batch_size = params.shape[0]
        
        # Move parameters to device
        params = params.to(self.device)
        
        # Encode to latent space
        with torch.no_grad():
            z = self.encoder(params)
        
        # Apply forward diffusion for half of the steps
        noisy_z = z
        for t in range(num_steps // 2):
            noisy_z, _ = self.diffuse(noisy_z, t)
        
        # Apply reverse diffusion
        evolved_z = noisy_z
        for t in reversed(range(num_steps // 2)):
            evolved_z = self.denoise_step(evolved_z, t)
        
        # Decode to parameter space
        with torch.no_grad():
            evolved_params = self.decoder(evolved_z)
        
        # Evaluate fitness
        fitness = fitness_fn(evolved_params)
        
        # Keep only improvements
        original_fitness = fitness_fn(params)
        mask = (fitness > original_fitness).float().view(-1, 1)
        
        # Combine original and evolved parameters based on fitness
        result = mask * evolved_params + (1 - mask) * params
        
        return result.cpu()


def test_diffusion_evolution():
    """Test diffusion evolution optimization."""
    # Define a simple parameter tensor and fitness function
    param_dim = 64
    batch_size = 4
    
    # Create random parameters
    params = torch.randn(batch_size, param_dim)
    
    # Define a simple fitness function (e.g., negative L2 norm)
    def fitness_fn(p):
        return -torch.norm(p, dim=1)
    
    # Create diffusion evolution
    diffusion = DiffusionEvolution(
        latent_dim=16,
        param_dim=param_dim,
        device="cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
    )
    
    print(f"Diffusion Evolution test:")
    print(f"  Parameter dimension: {param_dim}")
    print(f"  Latent dimension: {diffusion.latent_dim}")
    print(f"  Number of diffusion steps: {diffusion.num_steps}")
    
    # Test training
    num_train_steps = 10
    total_loss = 0
    
    for i in range(num_train_steps):
        # Create random parameter batch
        train_params = torch.randn(batch_size, param_dim)
        
        # Train step
        loss = diffusion.train_step(train_params)
        total_loss += loss
        
        if i % 2 == 0:
            print(f"  Training step {i}: loss = {loss:.6f}")
    
    avg_loss = total_loss / num_train_steps
    print(f"  Average training loss: {avg_loss:.6f}")
    
    # Test sampling
    samples = diffusion.sample(num_samples=2)
    print(f"  Sampled parameters shape: {samples.shape}")
    
    # Test evolution
    original_fitness = fitness_fn(params).mean().item()
    print(f"  Original fitness: {original_fitness:.6f}")
    
    evolved_params = diffusion.evolve(params, fitness_fn)
    evolved_fitness = fitness_fn(evolved_params).mean().item()
    print(f"  Evolved fitness: {evolved_fitness:.6f}")
    print(f"  Fitness improvement: {evolved_fitness - original_fitness:.6f}")
    
    return {
        "avg_training_loss": avg_loss,
        "original_fitness": original_fitness,
        "evolved_fitness": evolved_fitness,
        "fitness_improvement": evolved_fitness - original_fitness
    }

diffusion_results = test_diffusion_evolution()
print(f"\nDiffusion Evolution test results: {diffusion_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: NaN values in diffusion training
  - Check gradients with `torch.autograd.detect_anomaly()`
  - Monitor beta schedule values
  - Add gradient clipping to optimizer

- **Issue**: Slow convergence or poor fitness improvement
  - Experiment with different beta schedules
  - Adjust latent dimension size
  - Increase network capacity or depth

- **Issue**: Memory issues during diffusion
  - Use half precision (fp16) for large models
  - Implement batched evolution
  - Optimize network architecture

### 4.2 NSGA-II Optimizer Implementation

Implement NSGA-II for multi-objective optimization:

```python
import torch
import numpy as np
from typing import List, Tuple, Callable

class NSGAOptimizer:
    """Non-dominated Sorting Genetic Algorithm (NSGA-II) for multi-objective optimization."""
    
    def __init__(self,
                param_dim: int,
                num_objectives: int,
                population_size: int = 100,
                mutation_rate: float = 0.1,
                crossover_rate: float = 0.7,
                device: str = "cuda"):
        """
        Initialize an NSGA-II optimizer.
        
        Args:
            param_dim: Dimension of parameter space
            num_objectives: Number of objective functions
            population_size: Size of population
            mutation_rate: Probability of mutation
            crossover_rate: Probability of crossover
            device: Device to run on
        """
        self.param_dim = param_dim
        self.num_objectives = num_objectives
        self.population_size = population_size
        self.mutation_rate = mutation_rate
        self.crossover_rate = crossover_rate
        self.device = device
    
    def _calculate_crowding_distance(self, objectives: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Calculate crowding distance for each individual.
        
        Args:
            objectives: Objective values for each individual
            
        Returns:
            Crowding distances
        """
        population_size, num_objectives = objectives.shape
        crowding_distance = torch.zeros(population_size, device=objectives.device)
        
        # For each objective
        for i in range(num_objectives):
            # Get values for this objective
            values = objectives[:, i]
            
            # Sort indices by this objective
            indices = torch.argsort(values)
            sorted_values = values[indices]
            
            # Set boundary points to infinity
            crowding_distance[indices[0]] = float('inf')
            crowding_distance[indices[-1]] = float('inf')
            
            # Compute crowding distance for intermediate points
            if population_size > 2:
                # Normalize by range
                value_range = sorted_values[-1] - sorted_values[0]
                if value_range > 0:
                    for j in range(1, population_size - 1):
                        crowding_distance[indices[j]] += (sorted_values[j+1] - sorted_values[j-1]) / value_range
        
        return crowding_distance
    
    def _non_dominated_sort(self, objectives: torch.Tensor) -> List[torch.Tensor]:
        """
        Perform non-dominated sorting.
        
        Args:
            objectives: Objective values for each individual
            
        Returns:
            List of arrays containing indices for each front
        """
        population_size = objectives.shape[0]
        domination_counts = torch.zeros(population_size, dtype=torch.int, device=objectives.device)
        dominated_sets = [[] for _ in range(population_size)]
        fronts = [[]]
        
        # For each individual p
        for p in range(population_size):
            # For each individual q
            for q in range(population_size):
                if p == q:
                    continue
                
                # Check if p dominates q
                p_dominates_q = torch.all(objectives[p] >= objectives[q]) and torch.any(objectives[p] > objectives[q])
                
                # Check if q dominates p
                q_dominates_p = torch.all(objectives[q] >= objectives[p]) and torch.any(objectives[q] > objectives[p])
                
                if p_dominates_q:
                    dominated_sets[p].append(q)
                elif q_dominates_p:
                    domination_counts[p] += 1
            
            # If p is not dominated by any other individual, add to first front
            if domination_counts[p] == 0:
                fronts[0].append(p)
        
        # Generate subsequent fronts
        i = 0
        while len(fronts[i]) > 0:
            next_front = []
            
            # For each individual p in current front
            for p in fronts[i]:
                # For each individual q dominated by p
                for q in dominated_sets[p]:
                    domination_counts[q] -= 1
                    
                    # If q is not dominated by any other individual, add to next front
                    if domination_counts[q] == 0:
                        next_front.append(q)
            
            i += 1
            fronts.append(next_front)
        
        # Remove empty last front
        if len(fronts[-1]) == 0:
            fronts.pop()
        
        return [torch.tensor(front, device=objectives.device) for front in fronts]
    
    def _tournament_selection(self, ranks: torch.Tensor, crowding_distances: torch.Tensor) -> int:
        """
        Perform tournament selection.
        
        Args:
            ranks: Rank for each individual
            crowding_distances: Crowding distance for each individual
            
        Returns:
            Index of selected individual
        """
        # Select two random individuals
        idx1 = torch.randint(0, len(ranks), (1,)).item()
        idx2 = torch.randint(0, len(ranks), (1,)).item()
        
        # Select the better individual
        if ranks[idx1] < ranks[idx2]:
            return idx1
        elif ranks[idx1] > ranks[idx2]:
            return idx2
        else:
            # If ranks are equal, select the one with larger crowding distance
            if crowding_distances[idx1] > crowding_distances[idx2]:
                return idx1
            else:
                return idx2
    
    def _crossover(self, parent1: torch.Tensor, parent2: torch.Tensor) -> Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor]:
        """
        Perform crossover between two parents.
        
        Args:
            parent1: First parent
            parent2: Second parent
            
        Returns:
            Tuple of (child1, child2)
        """
        # Decide whether to perform crossover
        if torch.rand(1).item() < self.crossover_rate:
            # Simulated binary crossover (SBX)
            eta = 15  # Distribution index
            u = torch.rand(self.param_dim, device=parent1.device)
            beta = torch.where(u <= 0.5, 
                              (2 * u) ** (1 / (eta + 1)),
                              (1 / (2 * (1 - u))) ** (1 / (eta + 1)))
            
            child1 = 0.5 * ((1 + beta) * parent1 + (1 - beta) * parent2)
            child2 = 0.5 * ((1 - beta) * parent1 + (1 + beta) * parent2)
            
            return child1, child2
        else:
            return parent1.clone(), parent2.clone()
    
    def _mutate(self, individual: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Perform mutation on an individual.
        
        Args:
            individual: Individual to mutate
            
        Returns:
            Mutated individual
        """
        # Polynomial mutation
        eta = 20  # Distribution index
        
        # For each parameter
        for i in range(self.param_dim):
            # Decide whether to mutate this parameter
            if torch.rand(1).item() < self.mutation_rate:
                # Generate random number
                u = torch.rand(1, device=individual.device).item()
                
                # Calculate delta
                if u < 0.5:
                    delta = (2 * u) ** (1 / (eta + 1)) - 1
                else:
                    delta = 1 - (2 * (1 - u)) ** (1 / (eta + 1))
                
                # Apply mutation
                individual[i] += delta
        
        # Clip values to valid range
        individual = torch.clamp(individual, -1.0, 1.0)
        
        return individual
    
    def optimize(self, 
                initial_population: torch.Tensor, 
                objective_functions: List[Callable], 
                num_generations: int = 100) -> Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor]:
        """
        Optimize parameters using NSGA-II.
        
        Args:
            initial_population: Initial population of parameters
            objective_functions: List of objective functions to maximize
            num_generations: Number of generations to run
            
        Returns:
            Tuple of (best_parameters, best_objectives)
        """
        assert len(objective_functions) == self.num_objectives, "Number of objective functions must match num_objectives"
        
        population = initial_population.clone().to(self.device)
        population_size, param_dim = population.shape
        
        print(f"NSGA-II optimization:")
        print(f"  Population size: {population_size}")
        print(f"  Parameter dimension: {param_dim}")
        print(f"  Number of objectives: {self.num_objectives}")
        print(f"  Number of generations: {num_generations}")
        
        # Run for specified number of generations
        for generation in range(num_generations):
            # Evaluate objectives for current population
            objectives = torch.zeros(population_size, self.num_objectives, device=self.device)
            for i, objective_fn in enumerate(objective_functions):
                objectives[:, i] = objective_fn(population)
            
            # Perform non-dominated sorting
            fronts = self._non_dominated_sort(objectives)
            
            # Calculate crowding distance for each front
            crowding_distances = torch.zeros(population_size, device=self.device)
            for front in fronts:
                crowding_distances[front] = self._calculate_crowding_distance(objectives[front])
            
            # Assign ranks
            ranks = torch.zeros(population_size, dtype=torch.int, device=self.device)
            for i, front in enumerate(fronts):
                ranks[front] = i
            
            # Create new population
            new_population = []
            
            while len(new_population) < population_size:
                # Select parents
                parent1_idx = self._tournament_selection(ranks, crowding_distances)
                parent2_idx = self._tournament_selection(ranks, crowding_distances)
                
                # Perform crossover
                child1, child2 = self._crossover(population[parent1_idx], population[parent2_idx])
                
                # Perform mutation
                child1 = self._mutate(child1)
                child2 = self._mutate(child2)
                
                # Add children to new population
                new_population.append(child1)
                
                if len(new_population) < population_size:
                    new_population.append(child2)
            
            # Update population
            population = torch.stack(new_population)
            
            # Log progress
            if generation % 10 == 0 or generation == num_generations - 1:
                mean_objectives = objectives.mean(dim=0)
                print(f"  Generation {generation}:")
                for i in range(self.num_objectives):
                    print(f"    Objective {i}: mean = {mean_objectives[i]:.6f}")
                
                num_pareto = len(fronts[0])
                print(f"    Pareto front size: {num_pareto}")
        
        # Get final objectives
        final_objectives = torch.zeros(population_size, self.num_objectives, device=self.device)
        for i, objective_fn in enumerate(objective_functions):
            final_objectives[:, i] = objective_fn(population)
        
        # Get first front (Pareto-optimal solutions)
        fronts = self._non_dominated_sort(final_objectives)
        pareto_optimal = population[fronts[0]]
        pareto_objectives = final_objectives[fronts[0]]
        
        print(f"Optimization completed:")
        print(f"  Final Pareto front size: {len(fronts[0])}")
        print(f"  Pareto set shape: {pareto_optimal.shape}")
        print(f"  Pareto front shape: {pareto_objectives.shape}")
        
        return pareto_optimal.cpu(), pareto_objectives.cpu()


def test_nsga_optimizer():
    """Test NSGA-II optimizer."""
    # Define parameter dimension and number of objectives
    param_dim = 32
    num_objectives = 3
    
    # Create initial population
    population_size = 50
    initial_population = torch.randn(population_size, param_dim)
    
    # Define objective functions (to be maximized)
    def objective1(params):
        # Maximize negative L2 norm
        return -torch.norm(params, dim=1)
    
    def objective2(params):
        # Maximize sum
        return torch.sum(params, dim=1)
    
    def objective3(params):
        # Maximize variance
        return torch.var(params, dim=1)
    
    objective_functions = [objective1, objective2, objective3]
    
    # Create NSGA-II optimizer
    nsga = NSGAOptimizer(
        param_dim=param_dim,
        num_objectives=num_objectives,
        population_size=population_size,
        device="cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
    )
    
    # Run optimization for a small number of generations
    num_generations = 20
    pareto_set, pareto_front = nsga.optimize(
        initial_population, 
        objective_functions, 
        num_generations
    )
    
    print(f"\nNSGA-II test:")
    print(f"  Pareto set shape: {pareto_set.shape}")
    print(f"  Pareto front shape: {pareto_front.shape}")
    
    # Evaluate initial objectives
    initial_objectives = torch.zeros(population_size, num_objectives)
    for i, objective_fn in enumerate(objective_functions):
        initial_objectives[:, i] = objective_fn(initial_population)
    
    # Compare initial and final objective values
    initial_mean = initial_objectives.mean(dim=0)
    final_mean = pareto_front.mean(dim=0)
    
    print(f"  Objective improvements:")
    for i in range(num_objectives):
        print(f"    Objective {i}: {initial_mean[i]:.6f} -> {final_mean[i]:.6f} "
              f"(change: {final_mean[i] - initial_mean[i]:.6f})")
    
    return {
        "pareto_set_size": pareto_set.shape[0],
        "initial_objectives_mean": initial_mean.tolist(),
        "final_objectives_mean": final_mean.tolist(),
        "improvements": (final_mean - initial_mean).tolist()
    }

nsga_results = test_nsga_optimizer()
print(f"\nNSGA-II test results: {nsga_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Domination calculation errors
  - Debug non-dominated sorting logic step by step
  - Verify strict vs. non-strict comparisons
  - Add assertions for domination relationships

- **Issue**: Slow convergence
  - Adjust mutation and crossover rates
  - Implement adaptive mutation
  - Verify diversity maintenance

### 4.3 Training Loop Implementation

Create a training loop with curriculum:

```python
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import numpy as np
import time
import json
from tqdm import tqdm
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from pathlib import Path

class Trainer:
    """Training loop for LH-LLM with curriculum learning."""
    
    def __init__(self,
                model,
                config,
                diffusion_evolution=None,
                nsga_optimizer=None,
                save_dir="./training"):
        """
        Initialize a trainer.
        
        Args:
            model: LH-LLM model
            config: Configuration object
            diffusion_evolution: DiffusionEvolution optimizer (optional)
            nsga_optimizer: NSGAOptimizer (optional)
            save_dir: Directory for saving checkpoints and metrics
        """
        self.model = model
        self.config = config
        self.device = config.device
        self.save_dir = Path(save_dir)
        self.save_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        
        # Initialize optimizers
        self.diffusion_evolution = diffusion_evolution
        self.nsga_optimizer = nsga_optimizer
        
        # Create standard optimizer
        self.optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(
            self.model.parameters(),
            lr=config.learning_rate,
            weight_decay=config.weight_decay
        )
        
        # Training metrics
        self.metrics_history = {
            "train_loss": [],
            "fitness": [],
            "coherence": [],
            "phi": [],
            "avalanche_exponent": [],
            "energy_efficiency": [],
            "iteration_time": []
        }
        
        # Best metrics for checkpointing
        self.best_metrics = {
            "fitness": -float('inf'),
            "coherence": -float('inf'),
            "phi": -float('inf')
        }
        
        # Iteration counter
        self.current_iteration = 0
        
        # Curriculum stages
        self.curriculum_stages = [
            {"name": "cellular", "iterations": 200, "complexity": 0.2},
            {"name": "tissue", "iterations": 300, "complexity": 0.5},
            {"name": "organism", "iterations": 500, "complexity": 0.8},
            {"name": "consciousness", "iterations": None, "complexity": 1.0}
        ]
        self.current_stage = 0
    
    def _get_current_curriculum(self):
        """Get current curriculum settings."""
        if self.current_stage < len(self.curriculum_stages):
            return self.curriculum_stages[self.current_stage]
        return self.curriculum_stages[-1]
    
    def _update_curriculum(self):
        """Update curriculum stage if needed."""
        if self.current_stage >= len(self.curriculum_stages):
            return False
        
        current = self.curriculum_stages[self.current_stage]
        if current["iterations"] is not None and self.current_iteration >= current["iterations"]:
            self.current_stage += 1
            next_stage = self._get_current_curriculum()
            print(f"\nAdvancing to curriculum stage {self.current_stage}: {next_stage['name']}")
            print(f"Complexity: {next_stage['complexity']}")
            return True
        
        return False
    
    def _get_batch(self, batch_size, complexity):
        """
        Generate a batch of training examples with specified complexity.
        
        Args:
            batch_size: Batch size
            complexity: Complexity level (0.0 to 1.0)
            
        Returns:
            Dictionary of training tensors
        """
        # Scale sequence length with complexity
        seq_len = max(4, int(32 * complexity))
        
        # Create input tensors
        return {
            "input": torch.randn(batch_size, seq_len, self.config.d_model, device=self.device),
            "complexity": complexity
        }
    
    def _calculate_loss(self, outputs, metrics, batch):
        """
        Calculate training loss.
        
        Args:
            outputs: Model outputs
            metrics: Model metrics
            batch: Input batch
            
        Returns:
            Loss tensor
        """
        # Get key metrics
        coherence = metrics.get("coherence", torch.tensor(0.0, device=self.device))
        phi = metrics.get("phi", torch.tensor(0.0, device=self.device))
        avalanche_exponent = metrics.get("avalanche_exponent", torch.tensor(1.5, device=self.device))
        energy_efficiency = metrics.get("energy_efficiency", torch.tensor(0.0, device=self.device))
        
        # Target values from config
        target_coherence = self.config.target_values["coherence"]
        target_phi = self.config.target_values["phi"]
        target_avalanche_exponent = self.config.target_values["avalanche_exponent"]
        target_energy = self.config.target_values["energy_efficiency"]
        
        # Calculate losses
        coherence_loss = F.mse_loss(coherence, torch.tensor(target_coherence, device=self.device))
        phi_loss = F.mse_loss(phi, torch.tensor(target_phi, device=self.device))
        avalanche_loss = F.mse_loss(avalanche_exponent, torch.tensor(target_avalanche_exponent, device=self.device))
        energy_loss = F.mse_loss(energy_efficiency, torch.tensor(target_energy, device=self.device))
        
        # Combine losses with weights from config
        total_loss = (
            self.config.metric_weights["coherence"] * coherence_loss +
            self.config.metric_weights["phi"] * phi_loss +
            self.config.metric_weights["avalanche_exponent"] * avalanche_loss +
            self.config.metric_weights["energy_efficiency"] * energy_loss
        )
        
        return total_loss
    
    def _calculate_fitness(self, metrics):
        """
        Calculate fitness from metrics.
        
        Args:
            metrics: Model metrics
            
        Returns:
            Fitness value
        """
        fitness = 0.0
        
        for metric, weight in self.config.metric_weights.items():
            if metric in metrics:
                value = metrics[metric]
                target = self.config.target_values.get(metric, 0.0)
                
                # Convert to tensor if not already
                if not isinstance(value, torch.Tensor):
                    value = torch.tensor(value, device=self.device)
                
                if not isinstance(target, torch.Tensor):
                    target = torch.tensor(target, device=self.device)
                
                # Calculate normalized fitness contribution
                # Higher is better, closer to target is better
                distance = torch.abs(value - target)
                normalized = 1.0 - torch.clamp(distance / (target + 1e-8), 0.0, 1.0)
                
                fitness += weight * normalized.item()
        
        return fitness
    
    def _save_checkpoint(self, metrics, is_best=False):
        """
        Save model checkpoint.
        
        Args:
            metrics: Current metrics
            is_best: Whether this is the best model so far
        """
        checkpoint = {
            "model_state_dict": self.model.state_dict(),
            "optimizer_state_dict": self.optimizer.state_dict(),
            "metrics": metrics,
            "iteration": self.current_iteration,
            "curriculum_stage": self.current_stage
        }
        
        # Save regular checkpoint
        checkpoint_path = self.save_dir / f"checkpoint_{self.current_iteration:06d}.pt"
        torch.save(checkpoint, checkpoint_path)
        
        # Save best checkpoint if needed
        if is_best:
            best_path = self.save_dir / "best_model.pt"
            torch.save(checkpoint, best_path)
            
            # Save best metrics
            with open(self.save_dir / "best_metrics.json", "w") as f:
                json.dump(metrics, f, indent=2)
    
    def _save_metrics(self):
        """Save training metrics to file."""
        metrics_path = self.save_dir / "metrics.json"
        with open(metrics_path, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.metrics_history, f, indent=2)
        
        # Plot key metrics
        self._plot_metrics()
    
    def _plot_metrics(self):
        """Plot training metrics."""
        plt.figure(figsize=(15, 10))
        
        # Plot training loss
        plt.subplot(2, 2, 1)
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["train_loss"])
        plt.title("Training Loss")
        plt.xlabel("Iteration")
        plt.ylabel("Loss")
        
        # Plot fitness
        plt.subplot(2, 2, 2)
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["fitness"])
        plt.title("Fitness")
        plt.xlabel("Iteration")
        plt.ylabel("Fitness")
        
        # Plot coherence and phi
        plt.subplot(2, 2, 3)
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["coherence"], label="Coherence")
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["phi"], label="Phi")
        plt.title("Integration Metrics")
        plt.xlabel("Iteration")
        plt.ylabel("Value")
        plt.legend()
        
        # Plot avalanche exponent and energy efficiency
        plt.subplot(2, 2, 4)
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["avalanche_exponent"], label="Avalanche Exponent")
        plt.plot(self.metrics_history["energy_efficiency"], label="Energy Efficiency")
        plt.title("Criticality and Efficiency")
        plt.xlabel("Iteration")
        plt.ylabel("Value")
        plt.legend()
        
        plt.tight_layout()
        plt.savefig(self.save_dir / "training_metrics.png")
        plt.close()
    
    def _apply_            with_labels=True, font_weight='bold')
    edge_weights = nx.get_edge_attributes(tissue.graph, 'weight')
    nx.draw_networkx_edge_labels(tissue.graph, pos, edge_labels=edge_weights)
    plt.title("Cellular Tissue Graph Structure")
    plt.savefig("tissue_graph.png")
    plt.close()
    
    return {
        "num_cells": len(tissue.cells),
        "num_edges": tissue.graph.number_of_edges(),
        "avg_degree": avg_degree,
        "is_connected": is_connected,
        "output_shape": outputs.shape,
        "metrics": metrics
    }

tissue_results = test_cellular_tissue()
print(f"\nCellular tissue test results: {tissue_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**

  - Verify node indices match cell indices
  - Check edge creation logic in initialization
  - Test with different sparsity values

- **Issue**: Adjacency matrix inconsistent with graph structure
  - Manually compare graph edges with adjacency tensor
  - Verify adjacency updates after graph changes
  - Check tensor device placement

- **Issue**: Cell communication failures
  - Trace message passing through neighbor connections
  - Verify adjacency weights are applied correctly
  - Debug tensor shapes during communication

### 2.7 Neural Controller Testing

Test the neural controller implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController, StripedHyenaAttention

def test_neural_controller():
    config = LHLLMConfig(d_model=128, num_heads=8, num_layers=4)
    
    # Create controller
    controller = NeuralController(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads,
        num_layers=config.num_layers,
        use_hyena=True  # Test with Striped Hyena Attention
    )
    
    # Test input
    batch_size = 4
    seq_len = 16
    inputs = torch.randn(batch_size, seq_len, config.d_model)
    
    # Forward pass
    outputs = controller(inputs)
    
    print(f"Neural controller test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    
    # Check output dictionary keys
    print(f"  Output keys: {list(outputs.keys())}")
    
    # Check action probabilities
    action_probs = outputs["action_probs"]
    print(f"  Action probabilities shape: {action_probs.shape}")
    print(f"  Action probability sum: {action_probs.sum(dim=1)}")  # Should be close to 1.0
    
    # Test StripedHyena specifically
    hyena = StripedHyenaAttention(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads
    )
    
    hyena_out = hyena(inputs)
    
    print(f"\nStriped Hyena Attention test:")
    print(f"  Input shape: {inputs.shape}")
    print(f"  Output shape: {hyena_out.shape}")
    
    # Test long-range dependencies
    # Create input with long-range pattern
    long_seq = 128
    long_input = torch.zeros(1, long_seq, config.d_model)
    
    # Add signal at beginning and end
    long_input[0, 0] = 1.0
    long_input[0, -1] = 1.0
    
    hyena_long_out = hyena(long_input)
    
    # Check if end has influence from beginning (long-range dependency)
    beginning_end_similarity = F.cosine_similarity(
        hyena_long_out[0, 0], hyena_long_out[0, -1], dim=0
    )
    
    print(f"  Long sequence shape: {long_input.shape}")
    print(f"  Beginning-end similarity: {beginning_end_similarity.item():.4f}")
    print(f"  Higher similarity indicates better long-range dependency modeling")
    
    return {
        "action_probs_shape": action_probs.shape,
        "action_prob_sum": action_probs.sum(dim=1).mean().item(),
        "hyena_output_shape": hyena_out.shape,
        "long_range_similarity": beginning_end_similarity.item()
    }

controller_results = test_neural_controller()
print(f"\nNeural controller test results: {controller_results}")

### 2.8 Self-Organized Criticality Testing

Test the Self-Organized Criticality implementation with:

```python
from lhllm.models.graph_evolution_module import SelfOrganizedCriticality
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

def test_self_organized_criticality():
    # Create SOC model
    soc = SelfOrganizedCriticality(grid_size=32, target_exponent=1.5)
    
    print(f"Self-Organized Criticality test:")
    print(f"  Grid size: {soc.grid_size}x{soc.grid_size}")
    print(f"  Target exponent: {soc.target_exponent}")
    
    # Run system for multiple steps
    energy_means = []
    active_sites = []
    num_steps = 1000
    
    for i in range(num_steps):
        energy, metrics = soc.step()
        
        energy_means.append(metrics["mean_energy"])
        active_sites.append(metrics["num_active_sites"])
        
        if i % 200 == 0:
            print(f"  Step {i}: Mean energy = {metrics['mean_energy']:.4f}, "
                  f"Active sites = {metrics['num_active_sites']}")
    
    # Plot energy evolution
    plt.figure(figsize=(12, 4))
    
    plt.subplot(1, 2, 1)
    plt.plot(energy_means)
    plt.title("Mean Energy Evolution")
    plt.xlabel("Time Step")
    plt.ylabel("Mean Energy")
    
    plt.subplot(1, 2, 2)
    plt.plot(active_sites)
    plt.title("Active Sites Evolution")
    plt.xlabel("Time Step")
    plt.ylabel("Number of Active Sites")
    
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.savefig("soc_evolution.png")
    plt.close()
    
    # Get avalanche distribution
    bin_centers, counts = soc.get_avalanche_distribution()
    
    # Check if we have enough avalanche data
    if len(bin_centers) > 0:
        # Plot avalanche distribution
        plt.figure(figsize=(8, 6))
        plt.loglog(bin_centers, counts, 'o-')
        
        # Fit power law
        if len(bin_centers) > 2:
            # Simple linear fit in log-log space
            log_x = np.log(bin_centers)
            log_y = np.log(counts)
            
            # Fit line
            coeffs = np.polyfit(log_x, log_y, 1)
            exponent = -coeffs[0]  # Negative slope is the exponent
            
            # Plot fit
            fit_y = np.exp(coeffs[1]) * bin_centers ** (-exponent)
            plt.loglog(bin_centers, fit_y, 'r--', 
                      label=f'Power law: $\\tau$ = {exponent:.2f}')
            plt.legend()
        
        plt.title("Avalanche Size Distribution")
        plt.xlabel("Avalanche Size")
        plt.ylabel("Probability")
        plt.savefig("avalanche_distribution.png")
        plt.close()
        
        print(f"  Avalanche analysis:")
        print(f"  Number of recorded avalanches: {len(soc.avalanche_sizes)}")
        print(f"  Fitted power law exponent: {exponent:.2f}")
        print(f"  Target exponent: {soc.target_exponent}")
    else:
        print(f"  Not enough avalanches recorded for distribution analysis")
    
    # Check final metrics
    final_energy, final_metrics = soc.step()
    print(f"  Final metrics: {final_metrics}")
    
    return {
        "num_steps": num_steps,
        "final_mean_energy": final_metrics["mean_energy"],
        "num_avalanches": len(soc.avalanche_sizes),
        "fitted_exponent": exponent if len(bin_centers) > 2 else None,
        "target_exponent": soc.target_exponent
    }

soc_results = test_self_organized_criticality()
print(f"\nSOC test results: {soc_results}")
```

**Debugging Tips:**
- **Issue**: Avalanche distributions not following power law
  - Adjust driving rate and threshold parameters
  - Increase number of iterations for better statistics
  - Check boundary conditions in grid implementation

- **Issue**: System not reaching critical state
  - Verify energy addition and dissipation balance
  - Check toppling rules for energy redistribution
  - Debug threshold mechanism and site activity

- **Issue**: NaN or infinite values
  - Add bounds checking for energy values
  - Implement clipping for extreme values
  - Add safety checks in avalanche exponent calculation

### 3.1 Component Integration

Test integration of components with:

```python
from lhllm.config.configuration import LHLLMConfig
from lhllm.models.dna_module import DNAEncoder
from lhllm.models.harmonic_module import HPULayer
from lhllm.models.digital_cell_module import DigitalCell, CellularTissue, OrganismLayer
from lhllm.models.neural_controller_module import NeuralController

def test_component_integration():
    # Create configuration
    config = LHLLMConfig(
        d_model=64,
        num_cells=16,
        num_layers=4,
        num_heads=4,
        bioelectric_kappa=0.1,
        or_frequency=40.0
    )
    
    print(f"Component integration test:")
    
    # Initialize DNA encoder
    dna_encoder = DNAEncoder(config)
    print(f"  DNA encoder initialized")
    
    # Generate DNA sequence for cell
    dna_sequence = dna_encoder.generate_sequence("Test cell architecture", n_tokens=100)
    print(f"  Generated DNA sequence of length {len(dna_sequence)}")
    
    # Create digital cell with DNA
    cell = DigitalCell(config, cell_id=0, dna_sequence=dna_sequence)
    print(f"  Digital cell created with DNA")

        num_tissues=2, 
        cells_per_tissue=8, 
        dna_encoder=dna_encoder
    )
    print(f"  Organism layer created with {organism.num_tissues} tissues")
    
    # Create neural controller
    controller = NeuralController(
        d_model=config.d_model,
        num_heads=config.num_heads,
        num_layers=config.num_layers
    )
    print(f"  Neural controller created")
    
    # Test data flow: Controller -> Organism -> Tissue -> Cell
    batch_size = 2
    
    # Create input for controller
    controller_input = torch.randn(batch_size, 10, config.d_model)
    controller_output = controller(controller_input)
    print(f"  Controller output keys: {list(controller_output.keys())}")
    
    # Create input for organism
    organism_input = torch.randn(batch_size, organism.num_tissues, 8, config.d_model)
    organism_output, organism_metrics = organism(organism_input)
    print(f"  Organism output shape: {organism_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Organism metrics: {organism_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for tissue
    tissue_input = torch.randn(batch_size, len(tissue.cells), config.d_model)
    tissue_output, tissue_metrics = tissue(tissue_input)
    print(f"  Tissue output shape: {tissue_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Tissue metrics: {tissue_metrics}")
    
    # Create input for cell
    cell_input = torch.randn(batch_size, config.d_model)
    cell_output, cell_metrics = cell(cell_input)
    print(f"  Cell output shape: {cell_output.shape}")
    print(f"  Cell metrics: {cell_metrics}")
    
    return {
        "controller_output_keys": list(controller_output.keys()),
        "organism_output_shape": list(organism_output.shape),
        "tissue_output_shape": list(tissue_output.shape),
        "cell_output_shape": list(cell_output.shape)
    }
